<Author>kingoubleck
<Content>Quaint, friendly and perfectly located. We went to Amsterdam for New Year 2008 and decided to stay at the Hotel Nadia for the third time. Before considering the Hotel Nadia you must consider Amsterdam as a whole. It is a vibrant beautiful city but not the most accessible at times. If you are deciding on which hotel to stay at and are concerned about the size or layout of the hotel then you simply must realise that this is Amsterdam and everything is condensed.With that in mind on with the review....The Hotel Nadia is quite simply the most friendly hotel we have ever stayed in anywhere in the world. The staff are always approachable and will always greet you with a friendly hello. Nothing is too much to ask from them and they have given us some great advice and help over the years. When you arrive at the Hotel you will be greeted not only by a friendly member of staff but also a daunting stairway up into the main reception area. I can not sum up just how daunting the stairs are at first but as mentioned before this is Amsterdam and everywhere is like that here. But I promise you that you do get used to the stairs and the staff are always willing to shuttle your luggage up for you. Once you are up the stairs you are greeted with a complimentary drink (much needed!) We were also greeted in our room by a fantastic bouquet of flowers welcoming us back home and its really apt as staying here is like staying with friends more than staying in a hotel. The rooms are small (again like most hotels in Amsterdam) but furnished wonderfully with some really quirky features. Everything you need in your room is there (Shower, WC, Fridge, Safe, TV with tons of channels etc) but the best rooms are ones with a balcony as the view is tremendous as you can see the stunning Westerkerk from your room but also the canal that runs alongside the building. The location is perfect as its central enough to make most important sights a mere five minute walk (Anne Frank House, Red Light District, Dam Square) and also slap bang in the middle of two supermarkets and a load of little cafes and restaurants that are also reasonably priced as they are slightly off the beaten track. There are also some lovely boutique shops two minutes away along the canal. It is the safest hotel we have ever stayed in too, Amsterdam can be quite boisterous at times what with stag weekends etc but thankfully Nadia is a family hotel that avoids the usual tourist groups due to its location. The hotel manager is also a great security plus in the hotel as he is a lovely man but you certainly wouldn鈥檛 want to get on the wrong side of him!!Breakfast is more than acceptable offering coffee, juices, teas, bread, toast, croissants and various cakes. The breakfast room itself is a sight to behold as it is beautiful. We have dietary requirements when staying in a hotel and this was and never has been a problem for us in the Nadia. All in all I have nothing to say other than good things about the Hotel Nadia. If you are looking for a flashy sterile five star hotel then this probably isn鈥檛 the place for you.But if you are looking for a safe, reasonably priced friendly hotel with awesome five star staff and a wonderful location then I strongly suggest booking the Nadia ASAP. Just don鈥檛 book it when we want to stay here because I don鈥檛 think we could ever stay anywhere else even if it was a five star hotel for free! We would miss the staff here far too much and it would feel like we were cheating on them! That how much we love of this hotel.

<Content>What a wonderful place! A friend of us recommended us very warmly this family-owned hotel located very close to the City Center (Dam).Upon contacting the management for the booking, they reacted in a snap and in a very friendly and customer centric manner. Despite the busy season (Christmas), they accomodated our room wishes. The rates were very competitive, really.Upon arriving we felt immediately at home, the welcome was great, personnalized, focused on our needs. Small but comfortable and very clean (with all amenities), our room had a wonderful view over the Canal and the Westerkerk. The breakfasts were generous and delicious. Just a note (posted on the hotel's website btw) : this hotel is not really suitable for elderly or disabled people because of the steep access stairs. If you need a very quiet room, you can ask for a courtyard room (the inner garden is charming).Overall, we will go back to the Nadia Hotel without hesitation when we travel to Amsterdam again. It's our turn now to spread the word of mouth and warmly recommend this nice and wonderful place !

<Author>Abigail79
<Content>wonderfully charming place My boyfriend and I just stayed 3 nights at the Nadia and could not have been happier with our experience. The woman working the reception desk when we arrived was warm and helpful, and our bags were waiting in our room for us by the time we finished checking in. Our room was very small but the wardrobe and plentiful shelving made it feel bigger. The lighting and decor were both very cute -- overall it was incredibly cozy and comfortable, and it could not have been cleaner (same for the bathroom). The breakfast room was delightful, too -- especially since it was decorated for Christmas. There were several ladies working to make sure there was also fresh coffee and juice. The entire staff were always friendly and helpful -- they helped us arrange for a shuttle service to the airport at the end of our visit, and helped us down with our bags. Security at the hotel is very good -- they monitor the always-locked front door via camera and don't allow in anyone who is not a registered guest, so you can be comfortable that there's never anything too shady going on in the rooms around you. The hallways smelled pretty strongly of cigarette smoke at times, which didn't bother us since our room never smelled smoky at all. But people who are extremely sensitive to cigarette smoke might be bothered. Our room was on the interior side of the building (not directly exposed to the street) so outside sound was no problem whatsoever. I do think the walls between the rooms and the hallway must be very thin, because we could hear people passing by and/or talking in the hallway very clearly. It was never particularly bothersome but if we had visited at a more crowded time of year it might have gotten annoying. Though you can always sleep with earplugs.The location could also not have been better -- it is very close to Dam Square but just enough out of the bustle and mayhem that you are able to really relax. We discovered a number of wonderful restaurants and bars within a 5-10 minute walk of the hotel. Overall we were thrilled with the Nadia, and would definitely stay there again.  
<Date>Dec 12, 2008

<Author>sweetg12651
<Content>Great Little Hotel Just returned from an eight day stay at Nadia. This was my fourth stay at Nadia in two years. The hotel is very conveniently situated - 5 min. walk from Dam Square, 10 min, from Centraal Station, Tram 14 stops in front of hotel, the Anne Frank House is 1-1/2 blocks away. Although the rooms are small and the stairs are steep and numerous, the rooms very clean, and quite cozy. Each room is equipped with a fridge, TV, safe, and free WIFI . They serve a more than adequate continental breakfast in the charming breakfast room. If you desire a more substantial breakfast, Sara's Pancake House next door has wonderful pancakes and omelets. The best selling point for Nadia is the 4-star service you receive in this 2-star hotel from the wonderful staff and manager, Osam. They are most helpful in providing information about the city and no request is too much for them. They treat each and every one of their guests as royalty. I highly recommend Nadia Hotel.

<Author>dgitarts
<Content>Nice accomodations Hotel Nadia is a great choice for accomodations in a city known for lots of crappy hotels. Nadia is in a beautiful building a short 5 min walk from Dam square. You can pretty much get to every landmark in this happening city from Hotel Nadia within a 20 min walk, or even quicker from a tram that stops 2 minutes away from the hotel. The front desk is staffed 24 hours a day with very helpful personnel, especially Osam, the property manager.Though rooms are really tiny (expected for the price and for Amsterdam), there is ample shelving for luggage; every room is equipped with a private shower and toilets; free breakfast is sufficient and included in the price. The quad room has a spectacular view and lots of room to hang out. For the reasonable price and excellent location, Hotel Nadia is a very good choice for Amsterdam!

<Author>PG2220
<Content>Great Hotel and good location Stayed at the Hotel Nadia this week with 16 other people. When booking a hotel for so many people you have to do your homework and I trawled through tripadvisor and was concerned finding that the standard of hotels in Amsterdam had a lot to be desired and prices were really unreasonable. Then I came across the Nadia which had great reviews and good prices and within minutes of a reservation request online I had prices and availability confirmed and even a phone call. My only concern was I was unable to pay a deposit and I know I had confirmation e-mails but a deposit gives you that piece of mind (just a suggestion).Upon arrival and during our stay we were looked after really well so full marks to the staff - Thank you. As in all hotels in Amsterdam the rooms are small but they had everything you need for a short city break and most importantly they were very clean.Breakfast was standard continental and available for 3 hours.The hotel is located in a great location just a few minutes walk from Dam Square and all of Amsterdam's attractions can be reached easily on foot.One place you must visit is the Ice Bar - 15 euros and includes a drink, but its the experience of standing in a deep freeze with glasses and seating made of ice and you get great coats and hats to wear !! If you have spare time go on the half day trip to the windmills of Zaanse Sans and then onto the cheese factory (don't buy the cheese - if you really want some its half price at airport) and then to fishing village of Volendam. In these few hours you see the real Holland. Osam at reception can help you organise this trip.

<Author>IsabelllaB
<Content>Heading for Amsterdam? Choose the Nadia! I was headed to Amsterdam for an academic conference and, with no recommendations from the organizers, was falling victim to the pin-in-the-map method. My best friend's daughter, a travel agent, rescued me with the Nadia! What a terrific location: two blocks from the Anne Frank House, down the street from the gorgeous tower of the Westerkerk, and backing directly onto the famous Nine Streets. I found a delightful cafe with a tasty menu a few steps away (The Panorama), and a block beyond that, a post office (important to me) and a supermarche !! And just beyond that, the Dam itself. Couldn't be better--and the first day I walked along the Prinsengracht Canal from the Anne Frank House to the Rijkmuseum-- thirty minutes of wonderful scenes: that is, the Nadia is close to all the important Tram lines, but one can also stroll from its location in the Centrum quarter to the Rijksmuseum and Van Gogh museum in the Museum quarter.I paid around 100 Euros a night for my seven-day stay. My room was a single--compact, but everything well organized and placed: television; microwave; coffee machine--and VERY important for me, a truly useable DESK with an excellent READING LIGHT--so rare in any kind of hotel. The staff at the Nadia strives to personalize service; by day three, I could find my room key awaiting me at the top of the 37 steps to the reception area (this IS Amsterdam, after all--great for physical fitness!). By the time I left, I felt I had a personal relationship with at least four members of the staff (including the owner and not mentioning the two gorgeous cats). I travel alone to these conferences, and the Nadia made me feel I really did have a 'home away from home,' if you don't mind me sinking into cliche. A highlight was receiving a bouquet from the owner on the day I delivered my paper!If you are looking for a luxury hotel, the Nadia is not it--the fitness/spa aspect is the Stairs. But it you want a centrally located, reasonable, very pleasant and personalized hotel experience--the Nadia is for you! Happy Travels.terry  
<Date>Nov 7, 2008

<Author>Hollsx2
<Content>What a little gem of a hotel! We have stayed in Amsterdam many times before, at a wide variety of hotels, but this was our first stay at the Nadia .....and it won't be our last! From the very onset of our stay, the hotel staff were very welcoming and friendly and really couldn't do more for us. We arrived early so our room wasn't ready but the Nadia is more than happy to look after your belongings until your room is available. Be advised, like many hotels in Amsterdam, the Nadia has very steep stairs and no lift, but once again the hotel staff insist on carrying your cases up and down any stairs for you, making life much easier. Remember to leave your cases at the bottom of the stairs when you first arrive (reception is on the first floor) and they will collect them for you.The hotel is very well situated. It is directly across the street from Westekerk (near Anne Frank's house) and trams stop there regularly throughout the day (although Amsterdam is best experienced by foot - there are some great finds down the little side streets) It is a few minutes walk to some of the best shopping areas in the city.Our modest room was very clean, comfortable and had everything we would need for our three night stay. Breakfast (breads cheese, cakes, croissants, yoghurt, juice and tea or coffee) takes place in a lovely balcony breakfast room where again the staff are very helpful and friendly. We celebrated our first wedding anniversary while we were there and the staff left a beautiful bouquet of flowers for us - we believe it is the touches like this that make a hotel stand out amongst the rest and helped to make our stay so enjoyable. When we next plan a visit to Amsterdam we will phone the hotel directly for their special deals as advised by the hotel staff. A lovely hotel and great value for money.

<Author>intrepid_traveller24
<Content>A room with a canal view Located within 10 minutes walking distance of the Dam this quaint hotel offered us comfort and ambience. After roaming along the canals for hours it was such a relief to get back to our room. Here, we could could relax on our beds and watch the passing traffic. Boats, small and large, old and new, slid pass our window along the Keizers Gracht canal while bikes with odd attachments to carry kids or shopping plied the canal roadsides.Our room was clean, adequate in size, beds slightly narrow but comfortable with a bar fridge and coffee/tea making facilities which we did not have in most hotels in Germany, Switzerland and France. A substantial continental breakfast was included - cheeses, meats, jams, bread, toast, coffee, tea. We ate in a breakfast room high above the street with views to the canal. The staff were friendly and helpful. Nadia is located across the canal from the Westerkerk where a carillon rings every 15 minutes. We did have ear plugs but we liked the sound and it seemed to merge into the background after a day or so. We stayed for 7 nights. The cost of a room with a canal view is extra and you need to request this when booking.

<Author>Dave7702
<Content>Solid hotel, great location Hotel Nadia is an excellent hotel in the heart of Amsterdam, right around the corner from the Anne Frank House and within walking distance of numeruos sights including Dam Square, the RLD, Centraal Station, and countless shops and restaurants. I booked one of the doubles that comes with a balcony. Free wireless was also a definite plus. I booked my stay for 6 nights through the hotel directly and they respond very quickly. Note that they normally offer a 6% discount if you pay in cash. My rate was around 670E for 6 nights so a great price for the location and service.The onyl drawback is the size of the rooms, but a visitor should use the same mentality as in New York City...if you are spending that much time in your hotel room that the size of the room becomes an issue, you are not having a good vacation.In the end, safe, clean and amazingly reasonably priced hotel in the heart of Amsterdam. Can't be beat.Note that at the moment there's scaffolding and a large screen on the canal side...not sure how much of an effect this has but for balconies on the street side there was no noticeable difference as there is no screen.

<Author>Pices-Miami
<Content>Great staff, good value With the exchange rate what it is for us Americans, I was really looking for a good value, and got it at Hotel Nadia. And the staff is very friendly. As you'd expect, the rooms are nothing fancy, but provided a good sleep. I asked for a quiet room, and got it ! Much quieter than expected, given the buzz of the city, cable cars, etc. I liked that the rooms have a frig, TV, safe, and remodeled bathrooms. However, the shower head spray in room 518 is a bit interesting / difficult --- No complaints at all on the WC in the first night's room. (we started and ended our trip with 1-night in Amsterdam); As you have probably already read, there is no elevator. The staff helps with the bags, thank goodness. Please know for older people or those who are not active at all, the stairs can be tiring -- We were on the top floor; that's 73 curvy steps up. At 40 yrs old, I'm glad that I was hitting the gym, before the trip ! Of course there are rooms on lower levels, but still more stairs than one typically climbs in the U.S. It's hard for me to rate it, as my only other hotel experience (over the past 8-yrs) has been at a much more expensive hotel. For this category of hotel, I recommend Hotel Nadia to anyone looking for a value in my favorite city.

<Author>CanSwe
<Content>Adorable hotel in an Amazing city It was our first time to Amsterdam and we definately picked a perfect hotel! It was very central, a close walk to everywhere, but still very quiet. We had a corner room on the top floor, so we could see over the river and the church in front of Anne Frank's house. The staff at the hotel were very friendly, polite and helpful. They offered us refreshments from the fridge almost every time we came through. As well, they remembered which room we were staying in and had our key ready by the time we got to the office. They also let us use their own computer to checkin for our flight home.The breakfast was ok, the room was quite crowded but had a nice view. The room was quite large and very unique. We loved it from the minute we walked in. One of the most charming hotels we've stayed in. The only complaint I have is how uncomfortable the beds are. For that price, I truly believe the hotel should upgrade the beds. Then it will easily be a 4* stay. The stairs were not a problem for us, even after walking around Amsterdam all day.All in all, it was a wonderful stay and we will definately consider staying there again. Amsterdam was an amazing city too and we can't wait to get back!

<Author>bozhura
<Content>Central location, polite staff but equipment needs a refreshing The hotel has a very central location, which is very convenient for touring around the city. The staff is very helpful and polite. However, the rooms and the bathroom are really small and the towels and the bath curtain surely need to be changed with new ones. For the price we paid (over 100 euro per night), we surely expected more. Also, if you are disabled or elderly person, or with kids, this hotel is not for you because the stairs are very tough and there is no lift. Anyway, given the overpriced hotels in Amsterdam and the overall impression from previous visitors' remarks about the tininess of most hotels there, this one can do a job for a night or two.

<Author>DamLoverHalifax
<Content>Well recommended for a 2-star hotel - can't wait to go back ! Just had 3 nights with the wife at the Nadia and loved it.The hotel is very well situated for eveything really, just a short walk to Dam Square, The Jordaan, Anne Frank House, RLD, Spui square etc. Trams run directly outside the hotel and also just out of the hotel to the right for trams towards the museums and Leidseplein.The hotel itself is excellent for a 2 star rated hotel.The rooms are small, but we expected that and booked a room with a balcony so we could sit out with a coffee. I would recommend this, it's not that much extra.As has been said previously, the stairs are very steep, but the staff do carry your luggage up and down for you. We were also able to leave our bags when we arrived early in the morning and they were delivered to our room when we checked in later.Breakfast is included, which was fine for our purposes - a coffee and juice and maybe a croissant just to set us up for our next day out round Amsterdam. However, for me, the best thing about the hotel was the friendliness and hospitality of the staff. They were unfailingly cheerful, polite and helpful. On the morning of our departure the gentleman on reception even went and set up the breakfast room an hour early so we could have something to eat before leaving.We will be back next time we visit Amsterdam.

<Author>Americanfriends5
<Content>A Wonderful Place to Stay I was with a group of five couples that stayed at Hotel Nadia in early August 2008. We all loved the hotel. It is not for everyone but if you are looking for a well-located, clean, friendly place to stay, this is for you. If you have trouble climbing stairs you would be better off going someplace else as the stairs are steep and there is no elevator. The rooms are small but clean. The hotel staff is very friendly and helpful. I don't think any of us have ever been to a friendlier hotel. The rooms are small but have everything you need. We were there for two days before a cruise and had decided to put what we thought we would need for our Amsterdam stay in our overnight bags. That turned out to be a very good idea because of the small rooms. We stored the larger suitcase. We wanted to find a good, clean hotel that was well-located so that we could walk or take the tram and this was the perfect hotel for that. We also wanted something that was what we call a local type hotel and not something that was just like at home. Hotel Nadia was perfect and exceeded our expectations. We loved everything about it.

<Author>Riverside1971
<Content>Even better second time around Its the second time I have stayed at Hotel Nadia and I very much hope it won't be my last.I had a lovely stay, I was well looked after by all the staff.The hotel is ideally situated next to all the major attractions and only a short walk from the station.The hotel itself is small, however there is everything and more that you could possible need. The rooms are very clean and tidy, theres a good sized fridge, tea and coffee facilities, beds are very comfy. There is a safe in the room, however you probably don't have to use it as the security in the hotel is extremely good as the front door is always locked and you need to buzz your way in each time.The hotel dosn't allow noisy stag holiday makers which is good as Amsterdam has plenty of those, so you won't be woken up at 3 in the morning by a gang of drunken men. I suppose if you want a really quiet night sleep then you may want to ask for a room away from the main street.Overall a really brilliant stay and I look forward to going back again sometime next year.

<Author>HAPPINESSIS
<Content>Hotel Nadia - A Hidden Gem The hotel was perfectly situated for our needs It is on several bus/trolley lines and is within walking distance to many churches and museums on our list. There were lots of restaurants close by plus stores and stores and stores.The hotel is located above shops and the stairs are extremely steep so it is not the best place for babies or small children and individuals not able to climb a steep staircase. They do not have an elevator but do offer to have your bags brought to your room.Our room was a typical small hotel room - and we managed quite nicely once we realized just how much space we had. Breakfasts were great and the dining room is so pleasant with many hanging plants and flowers decorating the room.We felt that the hotel is a hidden gem because from the street you would have no idea that it even existed a floor above the shops.

<Author>farnook
<Content>Fantastic location, immaculately clean, tiny room! We stayed here for two nights last weekend. It's a funny looking place, accessed from a door on the street where you scale a mountain-like staircase to the reception. The welcome is super friendly, highly organised and we were checked-in and out on the town within ten minutes. We were also offered free drinks on arrival - nice touch. The room though was absolutely tiny. Bed pushed up against the wall and the smallest bathroom I have ever experienced. However everything worked and there were carefully thought-out features like hooks on the doors, shelves where there's no space for a bedside cabinet etc. The weather was extremely hot and the hotel has no AC but this was not a problem. It's an old, naturally cool hotel and the room was also kitted-out with a fan. We were also plagued by mosquitos on the first night - annoying but not really the fault of the hotel. Breakfast is included but hardly worth bothering with. Average coffee, juice and a mediocre selection of soggy croissants, bread rolls, cheese and preserves are all that's offered. The breakfast room is also ridiculously small!All-in-all I would recommend this place even though it's quite expensive for the facilities offered.

<Author>planeteer
<Content>Delightful gem We travelled to Amsterdam to see our son perform with the Halle Youth Orchestra at a lunchtime concert in the Westerkerk. The Nadia is a charming hotel, occupying the end part of a very historic building. The location is absolutely fantastic, with the Westerkerk opposite, Anne Frank's house around the corner and the stop for the Canalbus just over the road. We had read about the friendly staff before we arrived and were not disappointed. Nothing is too much trouble for this family. They are welcoming, provide valuable tourist information and go the extra mile to make you feel comfortable. It is true that the rooms are snug - my husband felt that he was in the cabin on a ship! Everything is there to hand though - tv, fridge, fan and a safety deposit box, which is invaluable in a city hotel. Everything is perfectly kept, with fresh towels daily. The owners seem to know exactly what makes a difference to customers and the service reflects that. Breakfasts were good, with fresh juice and the usual continental fayre. The dining room is in period style, with lots of plants and fresh flowers. It too is tiny for the number of rooms, but seems to be able to accommodate the people it serves and we never had to wait on the three days of our stay. What is not to like about the Nadia? The only problem could be the stairs for the less mobile. They are certainly a challenge, but help to burn off the calories and are good exercise! Staff anticipate difficulties and carry bags etc., so the only thing you have to worry about is yourself. This is Amsterdam and the Nadia reflects the typical style of the buildings! We had a lovely stay, would definitely stay here again and will recommend the Nadia to our friends.

<Author>CedarWych
<Content>Hotel Nadia: Lovely staff  We stayed 5 nights at the Hotel Nadia and had a lovely time.The location is very central, just a few minutes from Dam Square, not far (short walk) to most main areas and quite near the Jordaan district with its lovely shops, restaurants,  cafes, but far enough away from the late night noisy city-centre activity. The staff were lovely, exceedingly friendly  helpful. The rooms are small and the stairs are steep so be prepared, but this is a traditional Dutch building and is part of the charm and there's so much to do in Amsterdam how much time do you want to spend in your hotel room? You're provided with a free drink on arrival and any suitcases are carried to room so you don't need to struggle up the stairs with them yourself.There's no air conditioning, but electric fans are provided and putting the fan on with the window open made the room perfectly comfortable even on a hot summer night.It's an easy to walk to the central station but if you have luggage the tram stops is very close by.Breakfast is served until 10 and if that's too early for you, there are some lovely cafes for yummy Dutch pancakes very close by. You can leave your luggage safely in their secure luggage room after you've check out, which if you have a late flight means you can enjoy your last day without having to carry all your luggage with you.We will certainly stay there again.

<Author>Vikkioria
<Content>Much better than expected! I was worried, having never been to Amsterdam and staying in a lowly rated hotel, but the reviews from the travelers were good. I always trust fellow travelers over travel critics. I was pleasantly surprised when we got there, we got there way before check-in and they held our bags for us so that we didn't have to walk around the city with them and offered us complimentary breakfast even though we weren't checked in yet. The staff was amazingly friendly, everyone was very nice and gave us recommendations of places to go. The rooms were small with a tv, minifridge, and a private bathroom. They had the most amazing windows, I loved sitting on the window sill just watching the city in motion. The free breakfast was great and in a cute little room. The best part was the location. It was within walking distance of most places. If you are looking for a five-star hotel this isn't it, but if you are looking for a clean, safe, convenient, cheap hotel this is the pick!Warning: If stairs are a problem for you, don't stay here. Depending on you floor you will easily be required to climb at least 100 steps if not more.

<Author>Das24
<Content>An interesting, quirky, very friendly little hotel. Great location PositivesThe location of this hotel is perfect. 100 yards from Anne Frank's house and on the edge of the beautiful Jordaan area. Also only 5 minute walk down to the Dam.Really friendly staff, who thankfully carried our bags up and down the stairs, remembered our names and provided us with plenty of free drinks.NegativesWe had a deluxe room and it was quite small, pretty basic and the smallest single bed I have ever slept in (since I was about 5 anyway). Breakfast not overly exciting, but there is a great pancake shop below the hotel which I would recommend.The stairs are very steep (as I suspect is the case with many hotels in Amsterdam), no lift, not really a problem for us but would be if you had young children or weren't too mobile.Overall a nice little hotel, very clean, very friendly. I would def stay here again as it's a great location and the staff are so friendly. Rooms are a little quirky and small so don't expect too much but it is definitely value for money.

<Author>Safari-Family-Jambo
<Content>A++ Hotel Great hotel. I was looking for a quad room, reasonably price and a good location. The Nadia meet all my requirements. The room was a decent size with a private bath, refrigerator and a canal view. It wasn't fancy but was clean and comfortable. The staff is outstanding and very friendly and helpful. I had to book this room directly with the hotel. The internet travel sites I used did not offer an option for a quad room. I contacted the hotel directly and submitted a request for a quad room and the dates I wanted. They responded very quickly with a room rate. The hotel is in a great location - within walking distance of the Anne Frank house. The entryway has very steep stairs to climb and if you have trouble walking or climbing this hotel is not for you. Luckily the staff carries your luggage to your room for you! The location is great but it can be a little noisy because the hotel is located on a main road. One night I had to wear my ear plugs but the Dutch had just won a World Cup match and cars honked their horns and people partied until early morning! I really enjoyed my stay at this hotel and would highly reommend it.

<Author>Love2TravelWorldwide
<Content>Location Location Location! I just returned from my 4 night stay at the Hotel Nadia and I would recommend for those of you going to Amsterdam for a short trip of a couple of days, not for a long-term stay. The hotel team was extremely welcoming, nice, helpful, and funny. The location cannot be beat. It is central to everything. No need to take a cab from Central Station since it's (literally) a 5 minute tram ride with the tram stopping on the same street as the hotel. With the current exchange rate between the dollar and the euro, this is a great bargain. Hotel is very clean and has all the amenities a person from the USA is used to.But be forewarned that the room I had was small. I'm used to small, but this was really small. Thank god I had a room with a balcony (which I highly recommend). And the bed I had was lumpy, but was able to sleep once I found the perfect spot to sleep on.Overall, I would recommend this hotel and actually stay here again for any future visits to Amsterdam. :0)

<Author>TravellingScribe
<Content>Friendly, clean but not for everyone I stayed in a single room (with balcony) for 3 nights while on business in Amsterdam. Everything was spotless; there was good linen on the bed (2 single beds in my room) and good towels in the very tiny bathroom. I am used to the high price to quality ratio in hotels in Europe's major cities so was not surprised by the rather cramped quarters but felt I could have done better. The door to the room, for example, bumped the table when opened so couldn't open fully and the door to the bathroom was more like half a door, requiring me to turn sideways to get thru (and I'm thin). The stairs up to reception were, as others have mentioned, extremely steep and it felt like mountaineering to climb them. Friends staying in an apartment in Amsterdam had a similar situation so this is common in these old narrow buildings but I've noticed that some small hotels do have lifts.. The Nadia staff carry your luggage up  down but be aware that this hotel is not for everyone for these reasons. Extremely friendly staff on the reception and, like almost everyone in Amsterdam, they spoke excellent English. There was a long wait before I could get into my room which was irritating as I had business to do. I was invited to sit in the tiny breakfast room while, presumably, someone made the room ready. Not sure about this - it was never explained. As this was mid afternoon, I felt this was a slip-up on the hotel's part.Breakfast was fairly basic but included in the room rate so I can't really complain about that. You couldn't expect breakfast in this standard of hotel to be lavish.I did not particularly like the area in which the hotel was situated but I'd be hard pressed to say which would be a better area (except perhaps further into the Jordaan area?) In my opinion Amsterdam is a scruffy city and the charm of the canals is tempered by the amount of litter, graffiti, and the general down-at-heel look of the place and the people (inhabitants and visitors!). Just my opinion after a year of quite extensive travelling in Europe... and I thought the same when I was last in Amsterdam about 20 years ago. My husband and I are planning to return for a couple of days in October to catch up with friends from Australia who will be ending a Danube cruise there and I will be looking for another hotel. I don't want to be hard on the Nadia which is OK for its price bracket but I know that, with my husband in tow, we will need to move up a notch for him to be happy. We both like the old style of architecture and fairly small hotels so I am considering some of the other suggestions in trip advisor reviews such as Hotel Brouwer and Hotel Fita.

<Author>Ronale
<Content>Great service I had read a lot about this hotel on tripadvisor and had certain expectations. I was not disappointed. The hotel it self could be a standard Amsterdam BB. I have stayed in similar hotels there and know what to expect for the price range, which is a clean comfortable, tiny room with basic amenities. However this hotel is all about the little things that the staff do to make your stay pleasant. They generally seem to be interested in making your stay comfortable without seeming fake.A few days before I was due to arrive I emailed the hotel with a query and they actually called me on my mobile phone to respond. When we arrived early, they assisted with carrying our bags up the mountain (which is the traditionally steep stairs), they offered us free breakfast and throughout our stay they made us feel welcome without going overbroad. It was just right. I can tell they are the type of hotel that understand their various types of clientele and treat them accordingly.The only one thing I was slightly disappointed in was the lack of variety offered for breakfast. I stayed at a similar hotel a few doors down from the Nadia, and they had a wider variety including ham cheese, boiled egg and a toaster for bread. The breakfast at Nadia was even more basic consisting of croissants, rolls and bread (no toaster). By no means did this ruin our excellent stay, I was just expecting more as I had something to compare it to.I would highly recommend this hotel if you are visiting for a few days and do not want to splash out. It is by far the best in its category

<Author>Middle_East_Explorer
<Content>Very disappointing, poor value hotel I've traveled around the world and lived in many countries, and I have to say that the Nadia Hotel is one of the most disappointing experiences of my entire travel life. I booked two rooms, one for myself and one for two friends. Each room was about $225, so I expected far more than we actually got. The only way that I can describe the decor of the Nadia is that it reminded me of the many Intourist hotels that I've stayed at in the former USSR. This is not a compliment. Cheap furnishings, heavily-varnished woods, small TVs, and the worst of all -- a pervasive musty, rubbery smell. As many others have commented, the rooms are no bigger than large closets. The bathrooms are OK, but with extremely small sinks and no shelves. The breakfast was also very disappointing -- essentially various pastries, bread, one kind of cheese, juice, coffee, and tea. No eggs, no fruit, no yoghurt -- in short, nothing of distinction for the price.The staff seemed to be caring and well-meaning, but there's not much they can do to improve the experience given the overall substandard nature of the property.

<Author>TedUnitedKingdom
<Content>Good job we weren't health and safety inspectors! We had been looking forward to our three days in Amsterdam for months, unfortunately the hotel was a let down to our holiday. First off, the room was not ready when we arrived. After returning later in the day to settle in, we were shocked to find....1) The amount of steep stairs to access the hotel2) The overall lack of cleanliness- the room was literally caked in dust, including in the cracks in the wall. You were not only looking at dust through the window, it flew around the room visibly in the sunlight! The safe was covered in dust and so was the fan, and the carpet did not look like it had been vacuumed since it has been opened. 3) The size of the room- you could not fully open the door as it hit the desk, and you couldn't even get your case through! The walkway between both beds was literally a matter of inches.4) The beds: One's mattress was larger than the base so that it pushed you out of bed and forced you onto the floor due to such worn springs. The other was literally hanging out of the window and the blanket got lost down the gap! They seemed itchy and infested- the place felt alive with bugs and no matter how long you spent in the shower, you didn't feel clean5) The breakfast consisted of cold bread, crackers, and cake. Anyone with a wheat intolerance would go hungry! No hot food was offered at all6) The bathroom was like a portacabin but smaller, with a shower which flooded and a toilet which broke during our stay7) The TV remote didn't work properly and was constantly stuck on one settingWe were always offered free drinks from the bar, almost as if the staff felt embarrassed by the hotel. We also had our picture taken with reception staff with the promise that it would be emailed to us when we returned to England. However, since being back we have received nothing and feel this is the last insult from this hotel. DEFINITELY one to avoid for all travellers who like a clean place to stay.

<Author>Dazoli
<Content>Hotel nadia was great value in the centre of Amsterdam We stayed in Amsterdam for 3 nights at Hotel Nadia based on reviews here. A little apprehensive as we rang the bell of the tiny door in the street but our welcome was fantastic . We were a little early but were offered a cold drink, coffee as we relaxed in the breakfast room getting our first glimpse of the Amsterdam canals. The staff also insisted on carrying our bags up the stairs for us. Our room was small but very clean and perfect for our needs - it also looked out to the canal in the side street - the fridge also meant we could stock up on some food from the nearby supermarket for picnics by the canals. Breakfast was adequate - rolls, cheese, coffee, tea, croissants, juice. Perfect location with easy tram ride from station (the tram numbers are on their web site) and 5 minute walk to the main square, 10 minute walk to red light district and many restaurants and bars in between. Amsterdam is a very interesting and perhaps unique city and we thoroughly enjoyed our stay here. We hired bikes for the day from Yellow Bike and they pointed us in the direction of the farming area by catching the ferry across the water at main train station - spent about 5 hours leisurely exploring the farms, dykes and villages. Would thoroughly recommend this hotel and its staff who continued to be extremely helpful right throughout our stay.

<Content>Excellent Staff...Great Location...Tiny, but Clean Rooms I recently stayed at the Hotel Nadia for two nights, in a single and a double room. I have to say that the staff is excellent...better than most 4 or 5 star hotels. Just as everyone else has said, the stairs are steep (but manageable), the rooms are super tiny (but I was only there to sleep), and the breakfast is exactly what I expected for the price. I paid 80 euro a night and feel like the price is fair. On my second night the owner suggested that I move to another room. I was in a single on the 4th floor and my room faced the sun all day. He said a room facing the street would be much cooler...and it was! I didn't even have to ask to be moved. Everyone there was great!!! I am a female and was traveling alone. I always felt very safe and never worried about strange people in the hotel, as everyone must be buzzed in.If you're trying to save money I would suggest staying at Hotel Nadia. Just know that the rooms are small, but being steps away from everything more than makes up for it. I had a wonderful time in Amsterdam and should I ever return I will stay at Hotel Nadia! Bravo!

Some of the best pictures I've ever taken were on the balcony of Hotel Nadia! Even when I'm not lucky enough to get a balcony room, I really don't mind because I always have a room with large windows that open wide for fresh air, and let in lots of sunlight, which I love! The building itself is so charming and historic, I really feel like I am part of Old Amsterdam when I stay at Hotel Nadia! The staff is super friendly and attentive to my specific needs and requests. I always find the bathrooms squeaky clean and the shower very inviting after a long train ride. The beautiful breakfast room is a lovely indoor garden. It is open all day and night for guests like me who like to sit in peace and watch the water in the canal, or read a book and have some coffee. I always feel very welcome and comfortable at Hotel Nadia!  
<Date>May 9, 2008

<Author>DuValois
<Content>Doll house digs at down home price" The Nadia! Returned this afternoon from another delightful stay at The Nadia Hotel in Amsterdam. Received warm welcome from Osam and staff. As usual my bags were ferried up to the room by a cheerful staff member. Weather was beautiful and the room's balcony with wicker chairs was a great place to relax between trips around Amsterdam, sipping a cold drink and watching the people on the street below. On arrival you get a complimentary soft drink, and the Albert Heim market is down the block where you can stock up on juice and soft drinks to store in the room's refrigerator. I love the Nadia for it's lovely old exterior, it's quirky doll house sized rooms, elegant Victorian breakfast room, reasonable rates for a cosmopolitan city, and the very friendly staff who want guests to enjoy their stay. Holland is a country of small things, and the rooms at The Nadia are very Dutch! The value of what you get for the price is exceptional. I'll be back to stay in three weeks, and then again at Christmas.

<Author>Casbeth
<Content>Excellent service and location As the phrase goes, it does exactly what it says on the tin! Previous reviews were accurate: the stairs are steep and narrow, the rooms are small, but the service couldn't be better. A few people commented on how good it was to get a welcome (soft) drink on arrival. We were fortunate enough to stay during a mini-heatwave, and were offered drinks a few times on returning to the hotel.Location is superb, whether you want to walk everywhere or hop on and off the canalbus. (Highly recommended for a great way of seeing Amsterdam.) The Anne Frank House is just across the street, but beware the queues, which are very long, even first thing in the morning.Don't expect plush accomodation. That's not what you'll get at Nadia, but the rooms are cleaned every day, and the service is better than many more expensive hotels that we've stayed in!Definitely recommended as a base to see Amsterdam. Thank you everyone at Nadia!

<Author>stilletos
<Content>Read the reviews before you decide! We have just returned from a 4 night stay at the Hotel Nadia with friends - apparently we paid for a twin de-luxe room! The room was more like a corridor and there was no wardrobe or anywhere else to put clothes. My bed was pressed right up against the window, my husband was right up against a wooden partition - we had a 6 gap between the beds and it was impossible to walk in the room unless one or other of us went into the en-suite bathroom or sat on a bed. I think the room would be impossibly hot during the summer months, and we were unable to open the window except for about 1 at the top. There was a very small fan that was placed high up on a shelf and had no effect whatsoever. (A word of caution - if offered the key to room 7 have a look first before you decide). The stairs were certainly VERY steep but not too much of a problem and if I was strictly honest the plusses probably just about out-weighed the minuses. The staff were excellent, the breakfast was unexciting but adequate, the room was fairly clean and quiet, no passing traffic inside the hotel and there was not a great deal of noise from the street or canal. We are all in our 60s and I would not recommend this hotel for people who are not in reasonably good health and fitness (luckily we are!).

<Author>SJDub
<Content>Love to Lounge at the Nadia I will not be able to say enough about the hotel and the staff. Travelling from Nova Scotia, Canada, we arrived, and as advised, our bags were taken immediately to our awaiting room - 4th floor (top floor). We were greeted with a free non-alchohol beverage and very warm smiles. After a tour of the breakfast room, we were advised our room was ready. We were celebrating our 1st wedding anniversary and my husband casually mentioned this when booking the hotel, late in 2007. Though we didn't send a reminder, there was a fresh flower bouquet with a Happy Anniversary message from the Nadia. That was the first of many surprises.Our room was small, but the celings were very high, there was plenty of shelving and a closet. There was also an in room safe. The room was immaculately clean. Our bedspread had the most terrific message - Lounge. We had a balcony, which was a wonderful added touch -like another room altogether.The breakfast was a perfect start to the day - a variety of breads/pastry and cheese - tea/coffee/orange juice. Lots of choice for spreads - loved the nutella and croissants - and the coffee - Wow!The in room fridge was put to good use as was the in room kettle and tea supplies.There was a very powerful fan, for any one who likes to partake in the greenery of Amsterdam - this worked well to keep our room smelling fresh.The bathoom was also extremely clean, and the shower was powerful and HOT! Just the way I like it. The cleaning staff was excellent, even calling our room to make sure everything was okay.The customer service desk was open 24 hrs/day - with a buzz to get in rule, it is best to get a 24 hr hotel instead of one that will put a curfew on your evening out.Yes, it was rough to walk up four flights of stairs after a full day of walking but it was so satisfying to get up there and take a load off.I would recommend this hotel to any one who is able to handle the stairs. I must assume though, that a lot of the hotels in the area would have the same steep stairs.Thank you to the Nadia for helping to make our first visit to Amsterdam the best it could be. We miss you.

<Author>eni77
<Content>A Plsant Stay My friend and I originally booked a hotel, which is in the same building but 4 doors down the street from Hotel Nadia. But we had to move to Hotel Nadia because our booked room was too small. We were so happy we found Hotel Nadia. The staffs were super friendly and helpful with tourist information and day trip ideas. The room although small, can be considered a decent size, as in Amsterdam standard. The beds are very comfortable. We have a shower/toilet in the room, as well as a fridge, a safe, a TV and a desk with 2 chairs. Breakfast was served in a beautiful petit dining area on the 2ned floor. The buffet style breakfast isn鈥檛 fancy but has all the basic items. The location is perfect!!!!! A short 3 minutes walk to Anne Frank鈥檚 house and the trendy Jordaan neighborhood. 10-15 mins walk to Central station, Dam Square and Red light district. 15-20 mins walk to the museum area. I would stay at Hotel Nadia again on my next trip to Amsterdam!  
<Date>Apr 21, 2008

<Author>jenvalet
<Content>Fantastic Location, Friendly Staff Honestly, I'm kind of mixed about the Nadia. While I found the location to be perfect and the staff super friendly, the rooms are tiny (which I know is par for the course in Europe) and the beds were so uncomfortable - the sheets are like sandpaper. We had 2 separate stays while in town and the first half we were upgraded to the suite. I'm not sure how much that normally costs, but it was a good sized room with a nice view and a balcony. The stairs are rather daunting, around 75 total to the 4th floor, but it was our daily exercise. The second stay was in a room that was really small and almost had no place for 2 people to put their luggage, and we traveled lightly. The rooms were both clean and each came with a fridge, and coffee/tea maker, which was nice. The staff was always helpful. I can't comment on breakfast since we wanted to enjoy those delicious Dutch pancakes in town.If I didn't have to sleep in those beds again, I would recommend the Nadia. Again, the location can't be beat.

<Author>caffeinehit
<Content>Small but perfectly formed I have been coming to Amsterdam every week for some months now with work. It's really close and easy to walk to Centraal Station as well as all of the tourist spots nearby.All in all a very pleasant (and cheap) stay, I'm sure I will be back there.

<Author>blacknthai
<Content>Nadia Hotel....Love or Leave it? I've traveled throughout Europe quite a bit and stayed at several different hotels. I know that most older hotels in Europe are not as big as what we're accustomed to in the States, and prepare myself for this ahead of time. The Bad Stuff-The photos used on Nadia's website are very misleading. A panaromic view is shown which gives the viewer an illusion that the rooms are bigger. We had a triple room with a balcony. The room was ridiculously small! Two people would've fit comfortably in this room. The bathroom/shower was a joke! The shower leaked throughout the bathroom which made the situation even worse. If you're not young  in decent health, I would leave this hotel alone because of the most treacherous stairs! The Good Points-The hotel staff is most delightful! Not far from Dam Square  the Red Light District. The price was fair considering what we lived with for 4 days. If you don't mind being in small spaces, climbing like 80 stairs  sleeping on a rock hard bed with matching pillow, then this is the place for you.

<Author>Rosey21
<Content>Great staff, great location I stayed at the hotel Nadia for two nights with my boyfriend and really enjoyed the experience.We stayed in a double room with balcony, on the top floor. The stairs were a bit of a mission (but you soon get used to them!) the room was an awkward shape and the en suite made it quite small, but my boyfriend and i both felt the lovely view from the balcony outweighed these negative points.The staff on the front desk were lovely - we came into contact with three different people on reception and each were polite,friendly and very helpful in giving directions and recommendations.The breakfast was simple but adequate, and served in a lovely breakfast room with views over the canal and the catherdral.All in all, a lovely hotel with character and a great base for those wanting to explore amsterdam.**WORD OF ADVICE** there is an italian restaurant quite near the hotel called Venezia del nord...horrible food,atmosphere and service-i would avoid at all costs!!instead there is a lovely indian restaurant opposite catherdral which is definitley worth a visit!!Also, there is a airport shuttle bus, run by connexxions, which is a cheap and quick way to get door to door service between the hotel and airport.

<Author>sedap
<Content>Friendly, convenient, reliable (and small) I booked two nights at the Nadia in early April just 36h before turning up - it was one of the last rooms available in such a central location, just off Dam Square and in the Western Canal cafe and shopping belt.The hotel is in a building on Keizersgracht canal up some very steep stairs, but they'll bring all your bags up and down; and the rest of the time...I guess it makes up for the lack of a gym...and all those pancakes.The other downsides are that the rooms are tiny and they can be strict on the no-visitors rule. They are cosy, spotless, warm and quiet though. Also, the attention to detail makes a difference: the fridge is great to stock up on drinks from the nearby Albert Heijn supermarket, and the kettle was good for a cuppa coming in from the unseasonable cold. The shower heads are cordoned off quite effectively from the rest of the mini bathroom so the floor might get wet, but little else will. For the record, water pressure and heat were excellent - even on the fourth floor in the primetime chilly morning rush.Other perks included wireless internet and super management (welcome drinks, plasters for blisters, a toothbrush at midnight, taxi to the airport...you name it, it was taken care of with a smile).Summary: I had called a million places and Nadia's rates on absolute terms are about as low as Amsterdam gets. You might be able to find a larger place if you try earlier, but Nadia is tough to beat for convenience, reliability, friendliness and last-minute availability.

There were 2 flights of stairs which were quite high and very steep...we compared it to going up a ladder lol. However we were told to leave our bags there and to proceed to the reception area (at the top of these 2 flights).We were greeted by the owner who offered us some free soft drinks from the fridge in reception (this offer was made each time we returned to the hotel). Our room was then up 2 more steep flights of stairs and also at the front of the building. The owner told us that we could change rooms if we weren't happy. As the trams run most of the night it was quite noisy but we decided to stay as we were only there for 2 nights and just couldnt be bothered with the hassle.Breakfast was a substantial continental breakfast although the breakfast room was quite small and somewhat cramped.The Nadia was a cheap hotel so it's the usual 'you get what you pay for'! If you're anyway incapacitated dont dream of going here. If you're unfit like me and my partner go for the exercise lol!It's in a great location on the street at the back of the Royal Palace which is just a 3 minute walk from Dam Square.We would go back again coz we're not that fussy, it was ideal location, it was cheap and the staff were very friendly  
<Date>Mar 29, 2008

<Content>Nadia a great hotel Just returned from a great weekend in AmsterdamWe stayed at the Nadia Hotel and had a great time. This is a traditional Dutch Hotel that has been recently modernised, but still retains its original character.The staff are great, very helpful and friendly.the rooms are cosy  compact but have everything you need. <Author>gipi
<Content>Different, friendly, but bring your climbing boots! A lot of what I'll say has probably been said, but perhaps there's no harm in an update. The most recent trip was my second time at the Nadia, and I enjoyed it as much as the first time!A few observations, plusses and minusesIt's about 10 mins walk from the Dam and all the sights and sounds around there. It's less than 10 minutes to the Anne Frank House and other sights in that area.It's on the tram route for the Rembrantplein and the Zoo.The staff couldn't be friendlier and more helpful - from carrying bags upstairs, offering (non-alcoholic) drinks on arrival, providing maps  event guides, and making reservations for the hotel/airport shuttle, they couldn't do enough.The rooms are small, but comfortable and had all amenities - I was in a single room on the top (4th ) floor, and had a good size bed, ensuite with shower, TV, tea/coffee making facilities, safe and chair  desk. The room was spotless, and housekeeping called every day to make/change bed, clean bathroom, etc.The building is old and quirky - so you won't get a sterile square box to stay in. You may hear next door watching TV or....(well, it is Amsterdam!). You may hear your neighbours who've stayed out later than you coming home, saying goodnight and heading to bed.Yes, there are a lot of steep steps and no lift, so don't wear high heels and don't get too drunk while out for the evening! The staff will carry cases up and down, just ask!I asked for a non-smoking room, and was told they're in short supply - but I got one, so didn't have any difficulties mentioned by another reviewer.General noise - I was at the back of the hotel, so heard very little outside noise. Remember that you're in the middle of a city, which doesn't sleep, so noise is to be expected.I spent 4 nights here this time, and was very happy with the experience.Two tips- get the Conexxion hotel shuttle from Schipol to the door of the Nadia. Return fare is 鈧?1 and well worth the trip. You'll be dropped at the door, and the hotel will book the return trip for you. - Cafe Panorama, at the other end of the block is a nice place to eat (Italian pasta/pizza and steak).  
<Date>Mar 5, 2008

<Author>LondonMoxie
<Content>Think twice about this place We don't understand how this hotel got such good reviews on Trip Advisor - we only booked it because it did and were quite disappointed; now maybe will think again about the reliability of this site.Positive:* Staff very friendly and helpful at all times of day - in fact, they were too nice for such a disappointing place* Rooms well equipped and clean* Central location* Nice balcony (if you can stand the noise - see below)* Free drink on arrival (non-alcoholic)* Nice shower, in our room, at leastNegative (where to start...):* We had rooms at the front of the hotel which were very noisy - the tram rails were being changed during our stay, so we were woken 2 out of the 3 nights at 3 or 4am (I think that's what time it was) by the most awful noise that even ear-plugs couldn't block out* The hotel was very smoky - fine if you're out for a good time, but forget it if you have children, worth avoiding; everyone came back wheezing and coughing and we all stank of smoke of all types; people smoking in the middle of the night, smoke coming into room under doors, etc.* Breakfast was very disappointing - if you like cold croissants, cold bread, packaged rusks, packaged ginger bread and processed cheese (hardly what you'd expect in the land of cheese!) then you'd love it, but we didn't; no cereal, no fresh milk, no hot food (unless you asked for toast), no yoghurts, no fruit, nothing, even the bread was out of a packet* The rooms we had were tiny - no room to swing a cat; the only comparable thing is a berth on a ship and even then, we had bigger when we went to Santander by ferry; sitting on the toilet, your legs hit the door; also rooms very poorly lit* Expensive for what it was - we paid about 560 euros for 3 kids in one triple bedded room and 2 adults in a double bedded room for 3 nights and that included a discount for cash* TV was okay - lots of channels, but not all TV's received BBC - our kids room did, but our's not; CNN (puke!) was all we gotOther points:* Stairs - we knew there'd be lots, but 73 steps to our floor was a bit excessive, especially after walking the whole day (we were on the top floor) and all were steep* We're sure there are probably decent rooms in the hotel, but we didn't get them; perhaps a stay on the 1st or 2nd floor or inside rather than outside would be better - would recommend asking if you want to stay here* Stayed in much better places for much less money even on previous visits to Amsterdam. Would recommend looking for somewhere else and think about being slightly further out as that's probably what makes this place so expensive; think about a non-smoking place as well, you can always visit a cafe or a pub - they smoke everywhere anyway!

<Author>KansasTravelman
<Content>great little hotel this little hotel is great. first of all it has a great location just off the Dam square. right under this hotel,(as many are actually upstairs there) is shopping and a few good places to eat! When you first arrive there is a buzzer door you smile into the camera and they buzz the door open for you. in you go and the craziest stairs are right in front of you to the hotel level on the second floor. when you are arriving they send someone down to greet you and carry your baggage up for you as there is no elevator. up the stairs is the front desk with a humorous and very helpful staff. Of all the hotels i have stayed at in amsterdam, this one has had the best service.of course the rooms are tiny, but who needs them while in this cool city. they were clean and comfy and i had a canal view room with a spacious balcony for two or three even with chairs. I would certainly recommend this hotel and for the price you cannot beat it. - ABSOLUTLEY 1ST CLASS SERVICE, Thank you.

<Author>judith82
<Content>Loved staying at The Nadia! We chose hotel nadia based on their rates - they were the cheapest place we could find - and we were pleasantly surprised by its amenities. For a 2 star hotel, they offer many of the amentities of a higher rated hotel. We were greeted at the door with a smile, a porter took our luggage to the room. Our room was quite small - enought room for a double bed and not much else, but we had a balcony! We had a continental breakfast each morning we were there. The hotel is also extremely centrally locate. About a block from the Anne Frank House on one side and about 3 blocks from the Dam Square on the other side. Not to mention the fact that a tram line runs right outside. There was 24 hour front desk coverage and the hotel staff were able to accomodate every request we had. They aren't the most glamorous hotel, but I loved staying there, and I would recommend it to anyone, and should I go back to Amsterdam I would stay there in a heartbeat.

<Author>Corkonian0
<Content>lovely hotel, good location just back from 3 nights at the nadia hotel. couldn't really fault anything. yes, the stairs are VERY steep as mentioned previously, but we never once had to carry our luggage up or down the stairs.we were met on arrival and as it was too early to check in, our bags were brought to the luggage room and when we got back to the hotel later and went to the room our bags were already there.when checking out, they too looked after the bags and were downstairs ready for us to leave.the rooms are small but had more than enough facilities- tv,fridge,toilet/shower,safe,tea/coffee and hairdryer  irons were available from reception on request. would not think the room would be suitable for a girls weekend though - especially if your inclined to bring alot of baggage...location: 3-4 minutes from dam square and a further 10min from central station.the hotel is also on a tram route so all the major destinations/attractions are easily accessible if you don't fancy walking.the shuttle bus from airport to hotel is very handy-would definately travel this way again.staff very helpfull  friendly, received map of amsterdam and welcome drink on arrival. breakfast was typical continental style. some hotels charge extra for this.would definatley consider staying here again.

<Author>cim303
<Content>Pretty Good My first time in Amsterdam I stayed at this property so I don't have much to reference as far as other hotels in Amsterdam go. In terms of price when compared to other places I looked at, it was a pretty good deal. I felt that the location was pretty good as me and my friends were able to walk to just about everything we wanted to do. The staff are some of the nicest people I've ever dealt with at a hotel, I can't say enough about how welcome they made us feel. On a side note, I left my expensive iPod and Bose headphones in my room and I didn't realize it until after I left the city. I called them and they put the items to the side for me. I was supposed to arrange for a pick-up service to get the items mailed back to me but trying to get all of that arranged was beyond my capabilities at the time so unfortunately those items got left there. I kinda wish they would have just let me send them the money to ship the stuff back to me but alas... I hope they enjoy them!The room I was in was on the top floor and although extremely small (which I hear is the standard in Amsterdam) I thought it was clean and provided everything a twenty-something guy like me would need. The free wireless Internet was a nice bonus. I can't say much about the noise although I had a room that faced the street since I never got to bed until the early morning. Oh, the water pressure in the shower was good and the water was nice and hot. The towels provided are laughingly small but I guess I'm a spoiled American.The breakfast was pretty good. Actually, the best croissants I have *ever* had were there. Go figure, I couldn't find a better one in Paris.The stairs are freaking steep. I mean like almost straight up steep. Me and my friend who got there together laughed our [--] off as soon as we opened the front door to the place because the stairs were so incredible. The front desk guy came down and shlepped our heavy luggage up all of those stairs, totally nice guy, couldn't believe he did it.To sum it up, I'll probably look to go back to this place for my next visit to Amsterdam. The good combination of price, convenience, friendly staff, and decent accommodations is the catch here.BTW, too bad I can't add video to this review. I have excellent footage of the property, rooms and the experience with the stairs!

<Author>Greenmunkey
<Content>Nadia Hotel - Faultless stay I engaged in a considerable amount of research to find somewhere to stay in Amsterdam for a recent weekend in mid December. After reading the reviews, I settled for the Nadia Hotel. It is sometimes an all too often occurrence that people's expectations of some establishments are so high after reading a long tail of positive feedback, that even the slightest issue has a considerable impact on their perceptions of the place. However, the Nadia Hotel was absolutely faultless. Little touches like a free welcome drink and continental breakfast really do make a difference. The staff are excellent - all very friendly and eager to help in anyway they can. A good example is when I returned back late on my first night and mentioned that I couldn't get hold of any beers. Within five minutes there was a knock on my door with one of the guy's holding a couple of cans - which he proclaimed were on the house. The rooms, in typical Amsterdam style for establishments this size, are small. I opted for a single room with balcony, overlooking the bustling Raadhuisstraat. The lack of double glazing does mean the noise of traffic (particularly the trams), permeates into the room - but it is hardly a sleep killer!Rooms have TV, electronic safe, small fridge and tea/coffee making facilities. The bathroom is very small - yet adequate. Security is good, with a 24hr manned intercom secuity system, and older travellers ought to beware of the extremely steep steps that lead up to the reception and rooms. The location is, in my opinion, excellent. Less than 15 minutes walk from Centraal Station, or a mere 5 minutes from Dam Square - the hotel is ideally located for visitng the major sights of the city. The Nadia Hotel is an excellent choice for the single traveller who prefers the cosy atmosphere of a small hotel, and I will definitely be booking again when I visit the city again.  
<Date>Dec 19, 2007

My husband and i stayed at this hotel for a four day break.The staff were really helpful and friendly.As reported by other reviews the stairs were really steep no good for anyone with dissabilities etc.they are typical of Amsterdam buildings. The bedroom was small but who stays in their room all day .The sheets etc were crisp white cotton, towels changed every day.If you have a room starting with 4 look out you have 71 stairs to climb yes i did say 71 and they are really steep and narrow. The breakfast room is small,but quaint .We booked the shuttle bus from the airport for a return ticket it was 19.50(euros)a little expensive but you are dropped off at the door and picked up at the door so very convinient.Anne Franks museum is a must so is the Dutch Resistance museum. Fab location.Out of the door turn right 5 mins to the Dam (main square), where you will find the red light district and all the pubs.

<Author>fezman
<Content>great friendly service and staff, great location and room I found out a week before that I needed to be in Amsterdam for business for just one day. Since that was a Friday, I decided to stay through the weekend and enjoy Amsterdam (my second trip). My company was trying to get me to stay by the airport, but I did a little research here and found the Nadia.I emailed regarding availability and they got back to me quickly to confirm. Since I was travelling solo, and knew of the small rooms I picked the basic accomodation. I also added an additional day a few days before I arrived and was given no hassle at all.I arrived very late on friday following my meeting. Since it was late, cold and rainy, I took a cab from centraal station. Even though I knew the fare was escessive, and commented on it, I still got taken advantage off by the driver. Please beware of this!My reception was warm and I was offered a drink by the gracious man at the desk (sorry I didn't ask his name). He was very helpful my whole stay. The rooms are very small, but typical of the other places I've stayed in Amsterdam. Accomodations were clean and confortable, my top 2 requests. The bathroom was very small, it was hard to wash my face in the sink even!Very close to trams and Dam Square. Excellent location. I wouldn't hesitate to recommend this hotel to anyone. Although if you need western/'american style hotel rooms, you're best to look elsewhere. Thanks for a great stay!

<Author>HenryHopkins
<Content>37 Steps to Reception - Brings me "Home". 3 visits to Amsterdam this year and 3 stays in the Nadia. My first visit was in June when I booked a city break through a Travel Agent. I made my subsequent bookings on-line direcly with the Hotel.On the first visit I took a taxi from the Airport which cost about 鈧?0-00. The next time due to busy traffic and taking an alternative route that turned out to be equally busy cost 鈧?0-00. Third Time I took Train to Central Station for 鈧?-80.My first thoughts on arrival was:- there's the sign for the Nadia Hotel but where is it? The Taxi Driver rang the doorbell and when the door opened I was was a bit taken aback to see a really steep narrow stairway ahead of me. Maybe someone knew that the 39 Steps is one of my favourite films.Having overcome the intial shock, I made it to the Reception. Was given a Welcome Drink from the fridge and sat in breakfast room while my bags were taken to my room. (The hotel staff brought my luggage up and the down stairs on all my visits). I was also given a guidebook to Amsterdam 2007 and a leaflet about the Hotel. Had to lodge 鈧?0 Deposit for the Room Key /TV remote control - not asked for on subsequent visits.I did not read any reviews of the Hotel until after my first visit. Most reviewers comment on the friendly staff which I fully endorse. What sticks out in my mind was on Sunday morning when I asked where I would find a Catholic Church ,Osam (the Manager) was very helpful with directions and when I returned later in day the first thing he asked me had I found it.I stayed in a different room each time. One had twin beds. All the rooms I stayed in are all very small. Very Compact. Bathrooms also compact - Toilet -Wash hand basin and Shower. Wouldn't fancy it if I was any way overweight.I found the beds comfortable. Each room has a small fridge and safe. I did find that the safe was a little too high in my last room.One note of caution, mind the bed clothes that you don't trip.Also check if any small step from Bathroom to Bedroom.My most recent room had a balcony overlooking the street.There is a very nice Tearoom on the opposite side on the street called Jennifer's. There are a number ATM machines nearby,although one a few doors from Jennifer's did not take my type of card.I used the Shuttle Bus to return to the airport each time. The Hotel Reception did the booking for me.On my most recent arrival when I took the Train to Central Station, I had intending taking the Tram(which stops close to Hotel) but as it was a dry evening I ended up walking. Probably took about 15 minutes. On reflection maybe a bit too far to walk when pulling a suitcase.The Anne Frank House is only a few minutes away. Dam Square is about 10 minutes. One of my first stops there was Madame Tussauds.The Breakfast room is small. Even though I only have tea and toast at home when I go on holiday I like the Full Fry. So the continental breakfast is always a bit of a disappointment. Tea and Croissant still nice. It is not too difficult to find a restaurant around town that does the big fry. At breakfast, to make tea put teabag in cup and pour Boiling Water from Coffe Type Jug. If you need a bigger cup just ask.The Front door of hotel is always closed. Guests have to buzz everytime thecome in. You have to pass reception to get any of the rooms.Whenever I get back to to Amsterdam and as long as I (or if I should have a travelling companion) can make it up those steps anticipate I will be staying in the Nadia. (Where I hope to hear Osams words of greeting - Welcome Home.

<Author>Paula07
<Content>Hotel Nadia - Highly Recommended We stayed at this hotel in 2006 and were so impressed we booked direct with the hotel to return again this year, Nov 2007. The hotel is situated in a nice quiet area close to Dam Square and Ann Franks house. It is only about 8 mins from Central Station. The hotel is very clean and the rooms are cleaned daily. The rooms are not big but then if like us, you just want a base from which to explore this beautiful city, it is perfect. Our room had a TV, fridge, tea/coffee, shower, wc, safe and comfy bed. What more can you ask for ! The staff are all very friendly and helpful. It was my boyfriend's birthday during our stay and when we got back to the room on the afternoon of his birthday, there was a beautiful bouquet of flowers whishing him a Happy Birthday ! You don't get that sort of customer service very often !! We were really impressed. We checked out on the last day and the hotel kindly stored our luggage until late afternoon. Some guests have commented that the stairs are steep, I think there are about 37 up to main reception, but if you are fit and able, this is not a problem. Lets face it, with all the lovely food you will be eating in Dam, then a bit of exercise is a good thing !! I booked a room with a balcony on this visit and it was so nice to sit outside and watch the world go by in the mornings and the view is beautiful.
