<Author>OutandAboutAlaska
<Content>This place grows on you OK, here's the deal. After a flight from Moscow, a train ride, a tram ride, a short walk with a ton of luggage, I was pretty upset to see a dingy door leading to two flights of VERY steep and narrow staircase. No elevator. I was not happy (but very polite). Well, there was help. A small man told us we didn't have to worry about bringing our luggage up the stairs and that our luggage would be delivered to our room. OK, I'll buy that. After climbing the stairs we entered a very small and depressing receiving area - the front desk so to speak. Still not happy (and still polite-I do have manners). The man behind the desk took total control of the situation, offered us soda's and told us to wait in the breakfast room while our luggage was being brought up and our room was made ready. We headed down a poorly lit hallway with metal room doors on either side. Still not happy and wondering what we got ourselves into. We took a right and entered the breakfast room. Instant happiness! The room was everything you would want in an old European hotel. The room was small but very well decorated and cozy. There were large and beautiful windows and a door leading to a small balcony. I'm happy now. Anyway, the man told us our room was ready and gave us our key. We walked up two more flights of, again, VERY steep stairs. As we entered our room we were so very happy. It was the top corner room overlooking the canal and church. A door entered onto a small balcony and a set of half-moon windows opened to the canal and church. The room was extremely clean and efficient. High ceilings and everything you could possibly need to make your stay comfortable. The bed was very comfy. In the morning we returned to the breakfast room for the complimentary breakfast. The best croissants, jam, coffee, and juice. Again, very nice. The hotel is located near the Anne Frank house on a canal. I recommend this hotel ONLY if you want to brave the stairs. There is no elevator so you need to be able to climb the stairs. The staff at the hotel is far above average. So - excellent staff, great location, cool room, very clean. Give it a try.

<Content>Loved it! Highly Recommended! My wife and I stayed at the Nadia Hotel for two nights, having arranged to layover in Amsterdam on a trip back from Russia. <Author>Karospondent
<Content>Short break in Amsterdam Having read the previous reviews on this site, the hotel was much as we expected. The stairs are really steep (more like a ladder) and the room was very small but quite clean. The en-suite shower room was particularly small as was the hand basin in it, but if you want to stay in a budget hotel in the middle of the oldest part of Amsterdam this is what you get. The staff were very helpful and friendly and were able to answer all our questions like the best time to see Anne Frank House (we could see the size of the queue from our room!) and what trams to catch. We would rate the Nadia as offering good value and would be happy to stay there again.

<Author>pejpm
<Content>Hotel Nadia - Reccomended I stayed for one night in the Hotel Nadia on the 10th November. The hotel is in a fantastic location, only a couple of minutes from Dam Square, and close to the Anne Frank Huis. As with many buildings in Amsterdam, you enter via a very narrow steep staircase so the hotel would not be suitable for older people or people with disabilities. Upon arrival we were given a free soft drink, and were allowed to leave our luggage until our check in time later that day. The staff were all very friendly and helpful. The room was very small, but the bathroom was nice and the room was very clean. I stayed with a friend in a 2 bed room, and the beds were literally only 1 foot apart, but it was fine just for a weekend. If I were staying for more than a few days I would get a single room to myself. The hotel serves breakfast, although I didnt try it as we were more interested in exploring Amsterdam. On the whole, I would reccomend the Hotel Nadia to budget travellers, and short term visitors. For the location and price, it's hard to beat.

<Author>vedderfan23
<Content>Outstanding Stay My girlfriend and I just returned from a backpacking trip through Europe. We spent a few days in Amsterdam, and found Hotel Nadia via the Internet. We would both stay there again without a doubt. Yes, other reviews about the small size of the rooms are true, but we were only using the rooms to shower, sleep, and drink wine on our private balcony. Otherwise we were out exploring the city. The people running the hotel were the nicest I've meet in my trips in Europe. For instance, one night I went to the lobby and asked the gentleman behind the desk where I might find a store to find wine or beer at the hour of 10pm. He asked what I'd prefer - beer or wine. I said wine. He asked red or white. I said red. He asked that I wait a minute as he finished something behind the desk. He then got up and went out of sight, only to return 10 seconds later with a bottle of red wine. I asked how much I owed him, he said it was on the house. From helpful tips about the city, to comfort in the room, and transportation to the airport, our entire experience in Nadia couldn't have been better.

<Author>Grif_and_Whitestar
<Content>after 5 months of traveling it was like coming home! We decided this year to take the vacation of all vacations and left on a five month, around the world adventure in May, staying in all three, four and five star hotels for the entire period. The Nadia was the last stop on our last leg of a month in Europe. We booked it based on the reviews on Trip Advisor, because although it did not have one of the standard upscale brand names that are all over Amsterdam, the reviews were all outstanding. We were not disappointed! From the moment of our arrival everything was beyond our expectations. Although not a standard run-of-the-mill, modern five star hotel, the genuine hospitality, friendliness, attentiveness and service at the Nadia far exceeded anything we had experienced in places we paid four times as much for. Add to that a real classic landmark building two minutes from the center of town looking directly onto the canals with snarling gothic gargoyles leering down from the roof! The Nadia is the real deal! And those stairs! Don't worry, they will run your luggage up and down for you along with anything else you desire, but just experiencing those stairs took us back to the Amsterdam of the 18th century! I wouldn't pass them up for an elevator any day. Osam and his family make you feel like you have come home to Grandma's house. So if you want to experience the real deal while marveling at Amsterdam and be within two minutes walking distance from the Palace, don't take no for an answer and beg Osam for a room with a balcony!

<Author>bway2larj
<Content>Good break Amsterdam was OK for a weekend break - reasonably tacky, but tacky can be fun ! Loads of nice restaurants, and the native Dutch themselves are really friendly (can't say the same about all the nationalities there). Downside was graffiti everywhere, and by our fourth day (we were flying back in the evening) we were pretty bored as we had really done all the local sights and would have had to start travelling further afield. The shopping is pretty dull. So a two or three day trip max is good, unless you are planning on travelling outside of Amsterdam.The Hotel Nadia was nice and adequate for our purposes. Again, the staff were really friendly, and the room, although really small and dark, was comfortable and clean - the bathroom was very clean and well maintained, which was good.Nadia is well located - close to the shops and central Amsterdam, so we walked most places. Took the tram out to the museum quarter, which was a quiet area, so I'm glad we were more central.If we could ask for an improvement, then it would be stronger ligghting in the bedroom (we had a 'delux' room - number 5) and a more varied breakfast. Croissants and bread everyday gets boring fast. Again, adequate, but some fruit, yoghurt and cereals wouldn't go amiss.All in all, Nadia is a comfortable, safe hotel in a good location at a not unreasonable cost. Get past the initial impression that the front door gives you and the small bedroom, and you'll end up feeling that it is OK. We would stay here again without any problem.

<Author>7_Scottish_Ladies
<Content>Nadia Hotel is Superb. Great Location, Price, Friendly, Clean, Efficient I booked the Nadia Hotel for a group of seven using the hotel's website and found that the manager answered any e-mail enquiries very quickly and was extremely helpful.We had one triple deluxe room, a twin deluxe room and a twin room and all were clean, had en- suite WITH HAIRDRYER and well equipped with tea making facilities.We knew that hotel rooms in the centre of Amsterdam are compact, stairs tend to be steep and we had opted for this hotel knowing it did not have a lift/elevator and we just took out time going up and down the stairs. We were a mixed age group ranging from the age of 25 -60 years. Our luggage was carried up and down for us which was a bonus.The hotel was fully booked during our stay, so I advise you to book well in advance. Every member of the staff was extremely friendly and helpful and recommended the best places to go to eat and places to visit. The rooms cleaned and fresh towels every day.The breakfast was Continental style self service in a large room overlooking the canal. The choice of food was limited to various rolls, breads, croissants, jams and spreads and cheese but adequate as you could have as much as you wished and numerous refills of fresh orange juice, teas and coffeesOn our day of departure we stored our luggage in the locked baggage room and we were allowed to use the breakfast room as a meeting point and were offered refreshments.There is so much to do and see that a weekend was not long enough and we all hope to go back and EVERYONE in the group said they would definitely book the Nadia Hotel again!

<Author>muffinboz
<Content>Great Location, Friendly Staff Lots of steep stairs are inevitable in the older canalside buildings in Amsterdam, and this is the main drawback of this hotel. Room slightly cramped, but a wonderful canal view - and a LARGE double bed is not always found in Europe (it was more like UK King or US Queen size). Having a refrigerator in the room was also very useful. We had a problem at the end of the stay when the shuttle bus to the airport (booked for us by the hotel) failed to appear - apparently the booking was lost by the shuttle company. Hotel immediately accepted responsibility and ordered us a taxi to the airport (paid for by hotel). Generally an outstanding experience, with easy transport links and a five minute walk to Dam Square. Would definitely stay here again.

<Author>ChrissieWirral
<Content>Compact Nadia Hotel Experience! Hi. Just returned from weekend break to Amsterdam. Stayed in Nadia and had read reviews in advance - forewarned about small rooms and the stairs but going with logic it's only a bed, didn't worry unduly. Actually thought the stairs were great! Took a photo - just like lots of stairs in canal houses - made us laugh. We were a party of two couples - and were given two rooms - one double and one twin. It was pot luck, and when we went to our room, opened the door - I saw the bed an immediately looked for the other one - assuming we had the twin. There wasn't another one - it was a double bed and with a husband of over 6 ft - it's a good job I'm only small. It was the smallest room I have ever stayed in. The bed had to be that small, it wouldn't have taken another one. The shower was also dodgy. Difficult to get water temperature right - poor pressure - but it would suddenly go to scaulding hot which was a little scary. The good points were that it had a fridge -and a safe which was great. Also luggage care (we only had backpacks) was fine. Left them on last day and picked them up later. Very friendly people, breakfast okay - but get there before 8.30 or you won't get in. Good location - just by Anne Frank house - and pretty easy to get anywhere. Our friends room - the twin - was better. I'm sure ours was the smallest in the hotel. The photos on the website are taken at an angle to maximise space!

<Author>ziggymbg
<Content>Simply Remarkable! It is my great pleasure to give my review of The Nadia, a little hotel in the center of Amsterdam which provides to the traveler, if they are willing to be challenged as to what a hotel experience is usually like, an amazing and rewarding stay, a small, warm, humble, pleasant place unlike anyplace I鈥檝e stayed in. This is because of the intimate nature of the physical structure, the history, and location of the building, and the intimate nature of the hotel owners and staff. Now it鈥檚 very important to understand; this hotel is not for everybody because, and I like to think in a symbolic way, the two flights of very narrow and very steep staircases that one must climb up to hotel itself. If you鈥檝e stayed there you know exactly what I mean鈥his is an old building with no elevator so in order enter you must climb a big staircase. No joke. It like climbing a small mountain. But if you are up for the task and ready to climb the stairs to see what awaits you at the top then push the buzzer on the street go though the door and up you go! Warm and friendly faces greet you at the top in the very small cozy lobby. A smiling attendant offers to bring your luggage up the steep staircase. You are welcomed with a cold drink. Osam and his staff are ready for your arrival and they addressed me by name before I told them who I was. Osasm sized me up and gave me the loveliest room, #207 by the way, a corner room overlooking the canal and street. He gives rooms based on personal need and his expert knowledge of what room would be best for you. Don鈥檛 expect a luxurious room. Mine was small yet warm, with few amenities. (ok Osam, here is a negative, just like you wanted to know): the bathroom amenities could be greatly improved like better towels, soap, show curtain etc. It was clean but not fancy. Small but cozy. Trade in fancy for an historic building with years of history and personal service. It鈥檚 an old building and an historic monument so I take these things in stride鈥his is not a fancy place, it鈥檚 a genuine place and so some things can slip by. The personal service continued through my stay. Each time I returned to the hotel and by the time I reached the top of the stairs my key was placed for me on the counter. You leave the key each time you go out. The staff experience here is unlike any other. When was the last time you were greeted and attended to by the owner himself who is running the hotel from the big the long counter in the lobby. A place you must spend time in is the kitchen/ breakfast room. There you will find a tasty breakfast in the AM and coffee served all day and late into the night. One morning I ate some croissants and sipped coffee on the small kitchen balcony overlooking the street below. It was bucolic; a memory and feeling I will always cherish. My pleasant interactions with Osam the inn keeper continued my entire stay and during my last night I stayed with him talking for 2 hours and having the nicest exchange. When my cab came at 5:15 am Osam himself carried one of my bags down those steep flights and arranged a cheaper cab to get me to the train. I could go on about the guys who carry your bags up those long stairs and the kitchen staff, the magnificent view of the church across the street across from the Ann Frank House, the location, the location鈥? minutes walk to Dam Square, near all trams, near the quite Jordan and the 鈥? streets鈥?shopping area, an internet caf茅s down the street, good restaurants on the street, and a really tasty french fry cart right across the street鈥?and on and on鈥? but what makes this place great is what YOU can get from it. I will certainly return to the Nadia again when I visit Amsterdam. Osam has already promised me that if I want the same room, it鈥檚 mine although there are so many lovely rooms I might try something new. This is a marvelous hotel experience and should not be missed.

<Author>zsazsa123
<Content>Wonderful stay at the Nadia The staff was unbeatable at this hotel. I made a major mistake when booking the hotel, and ended up calling and trying to get two rooms for the very next day instead. Everything was worked out for us, with smiles! It is a great location with a restaurant closeby (turn right out of the hotel, go to end of block--good omelettes), and a pancake restaurant right next door. We were welcomed at the hotel with a cold drink, which was great after a 2 hour drive and the hospitality never ended. The room is quite small, and the reception is at the top of a long set of steep stairs, as people have mentioned. Good little continental breakfast was included with our rate, and the balcony off our room was great in the morning, watching the city wake up! The public transportation of trams was great and convenient for sightseeing, and our car was taken care of by a company the hotel works with. There is also a taxi stand as you go left out of the hotel, and just over the tiny bridge. A great stay at a great price! Pam in Brussels

<Author>Tarnie
<Content>Dinky Room! We stayed at the Nadia from 21 - 23 August. I agree with a previous comment that your heart does sink a little when you arrive outside the hotel and see the entrance sandwiched in a row of shops. My heart sank even more when we were shown to our double room which was really tiny with barely enough room for myself and my partner to move in at the same time. However, after the initial shock wore off we found the room to be more than adequate. The bathroom was small but clean and the shower was surprisingly powerful. Our room had a small balcony which overlooked the main road and canal which was very pleasant as the weather was quite warm. Although I didn't notice the noise from the trams my partner began to find them quite annoying!The staff at the hotel were very friendly and we were given useful maps and a guide book on arrival. The location of this hotel is perfect. We were able to walk from central station and from the hotel to Rembrandtplein, Leidseplein and the museum quarter. We didn't find it necessary to use either taxi's or trams.I chose this hotel based on the reviews on this website, the hotels location and the fact that I wanted to stay somewhere with a bit of character and not a modern chain hotel. I would recommend this hotel and thoroughly enjoyed my stay there

<Author>Beet7hoven
<Content>Highly recommended (with reservations - no pun intended) Arriving for the first time at this hotel your heart sinks (well, mine did, despite the positive reviews). From the exterior, it is unprepossessing - the narrow front door entrance is shoe-horned between a sewing machine shop (they still exist!) and a lighting establishment, with a protruding sign reminiscent of the Seventies. You press a buzzer to be let in and you are faced with a veritable Matterhorn of narrow, steep steps up to Reception. But, hey, this is Amsterdam, and that's how they made their houses. So either you will hate it already and wish you had booked a modern, purpose built, characterless concrete rectangle somewhere, or you will love it for its characterful, traditional appeal. I loved it.The Nadia occupies several floors of a sweeping crescent terrace, built circa 1890 and once elegant, but in need of the refurbishment currently underway. In its early days, part of it was used by the royal palace on Dam square, a few minutes walk away, to house its servants. At other times, it provided apartments for well-to-do middle class Amsterdamers, and had an array of useful shops at street level 鈥?one of which (no, not the computer outlet) still exists.Once you have scaled the entrance steps, you will more than likely be greeted by the owner himself manning the Reception desk who will offer a welcoming drink from the chill cabinet, proffer maps and guides and useful info, and, if your room isn鈥檛 ready, suggest you wait in the bright, airy and welcoming breakfast room along the corridor, overlooking the street below on one side and canal on the other and bedecked with plants and flowers.Judging by the brochure, the rooms are varied and quirky. I鈥檇 booked a twin for single occupancy, which had a (smallish) double bed and (child-sized) single bed. It was at the rear, looking out onto other apartments but suited me fine, especially as it was blissfully quiet, apart from the non-intrusive quarter-hour gentle bonging of a nearby church clock.With full occupancy of a (slim) couple and (well behaved) child it would have been a squeeze, with definitely no leeway for swinging a cat, especially in the toilet/shower-room which was definitely one person standing room only, but for a three-day stay (which, I鈥檇 guess is the average for most people visiting Amsterdam), it would be bearable for a two-and-a-half person family, and, erm, cosy for a couple. Think twice about demanding a room with a view 鈥?there could be traffic noise from the street below. Breakfasts at the Nadia are what you would expect from a typical Dutch hotel 鈥?croissants, a variety of breads and confitures, cold meats and cheese, coffee and a choice of teas 鈥?all help yourself, but with the lady of the establishment on hand in the adjacent kitchen. Anybody wanting eggs and bacon and hashbrowns and suchlike should opt for a concrete rectangle place鈥?br/>Apart from its welcoming atmosphere, cleanliness and quiet, the joy of the Nadia is its perfectly located central position 鈥?twixt Central Station and Rembrandt Square, and the Red Light District (should you wish its dubious delights) and the architectural jewels of the Westerkerk Jordaan quarter. Everywhere else is either walkable or easily accessed by tram, bus, or canal bus, or, if you must, wobbly (depending on your ability) bicycle. My reservations? Definitely not suitable for the infirm or anyone with mobility problems (as are many other Amsterdam hotels with walk-up, steep stairs), and, judged entirely on my own room, not suitable for the claustrophobic or any couple not on the best of terms鈥?And the lack of air conditioning could be a distinct drawback on hot nights (although my room had a fan strategically placed pointing at the bed. I wondered if the Red Light establishments had such luxury 鈥?I didn鈥檛 find out). Otherwise 鈥?10 out of 10 鈥?especially at the price鈥?br/>(PS: Bath mat, please, before my return visit!) (PPS: Beware Amsterdam taxi drivers. I was overcharged on arrival and short-changd on departure. They should be ashamed.)  
<Date>Aug 25, 2007

<Content>Excellent Nadia Hotel! I have just come back from Amsterdam, staying two nights at the Nadia Hotel, travellng with a friend. <Author>eindhovenaar
<Content>Enjoyable Stay We stayed for one night (July 3-4) at Nadia Hotel. We visited Amsterdam on July 3 and then left on July 4 to the Duinreserve (a lovely national park situated between Amsterdam and Alkmaar). Our stay at Nadia Hotel was an enjoyable one. As most other reviewers have noted, the staff were extremely friendly and the price, although well beyond average price for a 2 star hotel in the Netherlands, seems to be a norm in Amsterdam. The hotel is conveniently situated close to all attractions. The rooms are a bit tiny but the big windows openeing to the canal may remedy that (we got a canal-side room). One thing that may make a bad impression at arrival is the very steep staircase (typical Dutch) right at the entrance (leading to the reception) and the very narrow corridor to the rooms but overall, I was satisfied with the hotel and the rooms. The breakfast was ok; there was no milk, cereals or eggs but I guess you could order milk. You should also ask the waitress to toast your bread, if you want some. I was hearing the lady suggesting to another group of guests to buy some eggs and she could keep them in the firdge and cook them for their breakfast. All in all, there is not much luxury in Nadia Hotel but it has a very pleasant atmosphere.

They not only stored some of our luggage, but also had a Welcome Home bouquet for us on our return from Africa. The manager and his staff are extremely friendly and helpful and make every attempt to make your stay in Amsterdam memorable. The location is great with a bus and tram stop less than a block away. Even though this is a budget hotel, it is clean and is a great value, with many amenities. Yes, there are steep steps, but they provide much needed exercise for most of us. (There is always someone there to take your luggage up and down from street level.)

<Author>gqusaf
<Content>Good place to stay I stayed at the Nadia for a week (May - June 2007), in a double room with street-side balcony.GOOD POINTS: EMPLOYEES - Very courteous, always willing to help, including ordering food, giving directions, or anything that will make your stay more enjoyable. Absolutely professional and friendly! LOCATION - The hotel is only a 15 minute walk (5 minutes by bike) from the Red Light District, a 5 minute walk from the Anne Frank House. Major tram stop is less than 5 minutes away. SECURITY - Everyone who enters the building must be buzzed in by the front desk, and they have cameras all over the hotel. So no riff-raff hanging around inside, like some of the seedier hostels!BAD POINTS BREAKFAST - Left something to be desired...croissants, juice and coffee is about all you get. Also, breakfast is only served until 1030...if you party late and then sleep in, you'll probably miss it altogether. ROOM SIZE - The pictures on the website are misleading, as they shot them with a wide-angle camera...they are TINY! Not to be graphic, but if you are on the toilet with the bathroom door closed, your knees are hitting the door! I understand that tiny rooms are the norm in Amsterdam, but you will still be shocked when you see it! VISITORS - I'd like to see the no visitors rule softened...if you want someone to visit you in your room, they have to be a paying hotel customer to enter!

<Author>arodnick
<Content>A cozy well located hotel While I would not recommend the Nadia to anyone who is handicapped (very long and steep staircase), hotel prices are high in Amsterdam, and this was one of the better priced 2 star hotels. The rooms were small but clean and well appointed (including fans, which helped when it got hot), and the staff vere very friendly and attentive. We booked directly through their web site, and they responded promptly each time. When we arrived for our return stay of our round trip through Amsterdam, there were flowers in the room and a nice note. The breakfast is basic but adequate. The location is superb, right in the Jordaans district. For the price, I would definitely stay there again, but recommend a room without a view, as they are quieter. Amie Rodnick

<Author>marciabob
<Content>Good location - very small room The room was VERY small and bathroom L-shaped with the floor of the toilet and shower a few inches below the floor where the sink was. When you showered, therefore, the floor was also wet around the toilet. Upon arrival, the door was locked, and we later found out that you had to push the buzzer to gain entrance. Only a steep flight of stairs faces you with the reception area at the top. The friendliness and helpfulness of the owner made up for these disappointments. The small dining room was open in the evenings which helped as there was no lobby to sit in. It was straight to your room, otherwise, or stay out until you were ready to turn in. To its credit, the hotel was in an excellent location, 5 mins. from Dam Square. It is around the corner from the Ann Frank House and the Westerkerk church, the latter being seen from our small bal-cony.

<Author>VTMChris
<Content>Great Location, friendly staff! We were pleasantly surprised with this hotel. Amsterdam is VERY walkable for those that are fairly good walkers! ROOMS: Very small but cute and some rooms have balcony's, we really liked this feature, originally we had a room without a balcony and the staff offered to show us another room (which we didn't ask for, but was nice of them and we preferred the room with the balcony)! Bed was small, and space in the rooms was at a premium, bathroom was also small with one of the tiniest sinks I have ever seen, even in Europe. Rooms and hotel were clean and well maintained. Most channels on TV were in English with Dutch subtitles which was nice.BREAKFAST: The breakfast room was small but quaint. croissants, coffee, tea, orange juice, bread, cheese. It was adequate for our needs. The breakfast room has a little balcony that overlooks an intersection and canal.STAIRS: The hotel is on the upper floors of a building, you have to be buzzed in but the desk is staffed 24hours. The stairs leading up the hotel are intimidatingly steep, but they ask you to leave your bags on the first level and they we bring them to your room.The hotel is within two blocks of the Anne Frank house and three or four blocks of Dam Square. We were happy with the location and the hotel was quiet, we would definitely stay here again!  
<Date>May 26, 2007

<Author>Bosch116
<Content>What a special place! For the first time in 10 years we were going away without the children,and the Nadia Hotel,Amsterdam was to be our home for 4 days.Booking online via the hotel website was easy and there was always a prompt and thorough response to any enquiries.We were slightly daunted by the prospect of all THOSE stairs but,hey,they say exercise is good for you!!!On arrival at the hotel our fist impression wascan this ordinary looking front door in amongst a row of shops really be our hotel entrance?But,on that door being opened and seeing THOSE stairs we knew this was it!Our bags were carried up for us by a very friendly chap,and as we entered the reception we were greeted with a very warm welcome from Osam and his receptionist who immediately offered us a drink on the house.After a short while relaxing in the breakfast room we were directed to our room,which was small and basic,but was clean,comfortable,en-suite and had a lovely view of the canal and church.Having a fridge in the room was good for keeping the Heineken chilled(recommend anyone to do the Heineken Experience,great fun!)Also,satellite tv was provided which included BBC so we even watched Eastenders and match of the day!We also had tea/coffee facilities.Breakfast was a simple selection of continental usuals-croissants,jam,cake,bread,cheese,coffee,tea,juice.All self service so you could fill up before heading out and about.Osam and his staff were all so friendly and helpful we almost immediately felt as though we had known them for years(this feeling was only reinforced when on my birthday,the day after we retuned home,a message was left on our answer phone wishing me a happy birthday from all at the Nadia!)Their advice was a key factor in our ability to see and do so much in the short time we were in Amsterdam.The Hotels central location combined with the wonderful staff made this,in our opinion,the perfect accomodation.Try it for yourself-you'll love it too :-)

<Author>Lisa_DHoboken
<Content>Feel at home in the Nadia Hotel I just returned from a wonderful trip to Amsterdam, many of my fondest memories include the Nadia Hotel. Our decision to book at theNadia had much to do with the competitive rates, but mostly the glowing reviews. The Nadia Hotel lived up to every wonderful thing we have read. The staff is warm, friendly and accomodating. The owner, Osam is special in his own right. He makes you feel as though you are the only guest and your happiness and comfort is his priority. He adds personal touches similar to what you would experience in a bed and breakfast. My favorite memory of Osam is being invited to the kitchenas he made me a pot of coffee 2 hours before breakfast even began. We had many fantastic conversations with Osam that again, are as memorable as Amsterdam itself.The past reviews have mentioned the stairs, yes there is a bit of a climb which before arrival, we worried about, however, the anticipation far exceeded the reality. We saw guests young, old and even disabled climb the stairs to reception - use your judgement based on your own physical capabilities.There was a specific review mentioning room 316, that it was small, dirty, with an odor. <Content>Very Enjoyable Am just back from a terrific weekend in Amsterdam where we stayed 2 nights at the Nadia hotel. <Author>amsterdammers
<Content>4th time around Me and my boyfriend have made amsterdam a yearly break and we always stay at the Nadia. Its perfect for us!Dam square is a 10 minute walk away ( a lady never rushes! ) and its on an easy to find road - this is a bonus when its your first time in amsterdam and you've got lost and your trying to find your hotel. Its round the corner from the anne Frank house and there is a canal bus stop opposite- bonus!The staff are friendly and there is always someone at the desk. The stairs are really steep to get up to the hotel so i wouldnt suggest going there if you have a disability or have troubles with stairs.The rooms are clean. Small but cosy. They are en suite and the bathroos are also small but again clean, and the shower doesnt trickle. The double beds are huge and really comfy and you have a safety deposit box, a fridge and a TV in your room. You also have tea facilities in your room, and as every self respecting brit knows a good cup of tea at the end of a long day is well appreciated. Breakfast is served in a quaint little room with a view over the canal and the church. You have a choice of juice, tea, coffee, croissants, bread, toast, cheese, cakes and jams. Its not a full english, but its continental and adds to the experience of a european break.I could not fault this hotel and could not ask for more from a hotel- its safe, friendly, clean, cosy, reasonably priced in an excellent location - i would highly recomend it.

<Author>foxy12
<Content>Friendly and Helpful Nadia Hotel Myself and five others have just returned from a long weekend in Amsterdam staying at the Hotel Nadia. I found it by surfing around and the Hotel fit the bill. On arrival we were more than impressed by the friendliness of the staff and a welcome drink was waiting for us before we unpacked.The Hotel is on a Bed and Breakfast basis, the breakfast room overlooking one of the lovely canals. The Hotel is nicely situated not far from Dam Square and all attractions were easily accessable from the Hotel. But if you do not like walking, a tram stop is situated just opposite and very handy for anywhere in the City.We enquired several times for the location of different places and each time the staff on duty were extremely helpful and we were directed the best way to get to the destinations and therefore made our holiday stress free.The stairs were steep (as in all of Amsterdam's hotels) and there was no lift - BUT this did not deter us and was not a problem. In any case staff were on call at all times to help, should you need it, to take your luggage or bags up and down the stairs.I would throughly recommend Hotel Nadia to anyone planning a stay in Amsterdam.

<Content>WHAT A LET DOWN! I booked this hotel because of the good reviews it has on this sight and I ended up extremley dissapointed!!Yes the location is very good and yes the staff are friendly (which you should expect at a hotel anyway!), but the hotel isn't anything special. I had done my research before we arrived and i was expecting a small room and steep staircases. But the rooms aren't just small they are TINY. We had a room at the back of the hotel and you could actually stretch your arms out and touch the walls on each side. The bathroom was even smaller. I dont consider myself to be fussy but these rooms shouldn't be commissioned by the hotel as they are unbearable. I would have struggled to feel comfortable if i had stayed in the room alone because of the size, but with my boyfriend in there too we were constantly bumping into eachother. We couldnt be moved as the hotel was fully booked. We caught a glimpse of rooms at the front of the hotel when the maid was cleaning and they looked much bigger and much more comfortable so maby we were very unlucky. Advice for future guests AVOID ROOM 316.Also a horrible smell kept wafting from the bathroom, like sewage/ drains. It was like we could smell poo coming from the toilet when it hadn't been used! Not very nice. I wouldn't say that the hotel was particulaly clean either, the bin in our room was still full with the lasts guests rubbish when we arrived and the sheets looked as through they had been used since the 1970's. The hotel smelled a bit musty, it wasn't filthy but I think the standards could be improved. I wouldn't reccommend this hotel, and I wouldn't go again. Amsterdam on the other hand was brilliant and we will return.

<Content>Lovely Hotel and well placed within Amsterdam City Centre We have just arrived back after staying for 3 nights in Hotel Nadia. Hotel Nadia is nicely placed within the city as everything is within easy reach and a short distance away whether you choose to get there on foot, canal bus or tram. <Author>ajpimentel
<Content>Excellent!!! My wife and I stayed for two days at Nadia Hotel and we had a wonderful experience. It is the most friendly hotel we have ever been. Osam (manager) and Michelle (staff member) found out that it was our wedding anyversary and they even sent us flowers to our room! They gave us a lot of usefull and unbiased information, so we did not have any problem in finding good restaurants with rasonable prices, sightseeing boat tours, getting around the city and so on. The hotel has one of the most espetacular views of the city. You can even see a canal and an old cathedral from your bed. The hotel location could not be better. It is only a couple of blocks away from the most important museums and from the Dam square (center square of the city).It is true that the hotel has small rooms and that you have to climb very narow and high stairs, but unless you are an erderly person, this should be not a problem, the hotel's hospitaliy, location and excellency will more than compensate for these minor inconviniences.The hotel its above its range. <Author>iclaudius
<Content>"Charming" and "Romantic" might be cliche, but ... For a hotel stay i booked solely from reviews and photos on the internet, i'd say i outdid myself. my husband and i booked room #413 -- an extremely cozy, yet romantic double room with high ceilings, low lighting and stone balcony overlooking the busy street below. if you look at the front image of the hotel, it is the balcony room just by the N in the sign. since it is a corner room, it also has a pretty window overlooking westkerk cathedral and the canal. bathroom was small but updated and clean ... there was a place for everything. we didnt spend tons of time in the room however, since the hotel is located within walking distance to everything ....there is a particularly cool restaurant-cafe, panorama, on the corner.as for the staff, they were the friendliest that ive encountered in a long time,anywhere. the breakfast room, which is absolutely charming, especially on those dark chilly mornings in winter, was decorated for the holidays and provided a lovely starting point to every day ... thank you, nadia for a wonderful first experience in amsterdam!Arlington, VaUSA

<Author>Tipsymazuk
<Content>Beautiful historic hotel in a perfect location First, take a look at the hotel's website. It is beautifully composed and will give you a good insight into your stay at the Nadia. From the moment we arrived we were made to feel extremely welcome and yes, the room was small, but adequate for two of us. In fact, it was cosy, intimate and in character with the rest of the building, which is historic and should never be modernised. I do have problems with my knees and was apprehensive about the stairs, but there is a hand rail on each wall and I managed them better than I had hoped. Just be careful as the steps are narrow. There is a small landing halfway up the staircase, which is good for an oxygen intake!The breakfast room is one of the prettiest I have ever seen. Sadly, the breakfast itself comprised only of bread, cake, croissants and various jams. I feel some cold meat and eggs would have been a nice addition. The room itself was decorated in dark wood paneling, with lots of shelves and a small, but very functional bathroom. It was very warm however, so we kept the window open at all times. Please be aware that trams run constantly and love to ring their bells and the church opposite chimes every 15 minutes. The beds were very, very narrow and extremely uncomfortable. We spent each night clinging onto the mattress for fear of falling onto the floor. Regarding cleanliness, the hotel was spotless and we were asked each day if we would like housekeeping to tidy our room. Despite the poor beds and lack of a decent breakfast, this is a lovely hotel, with friendly staff, in a fantastic location. Amsterdam is a beautiful, friendly, relaxed and fun place to be and I would challenge anyone to visit the city and not have a good time.For something a little different, visit De Efteling which is an amazing fairytale themed park. It is an hour train ride from Central Station, then approximately 50 minutes by bus. We went to visit the Winter Wonderland that they do for Christmas, and it was absolutely perfect. Fake snow, real bonfires, warme chocolade melk and hot waffles. Fantastic!  
<Date>Dec 14, 2006

<Author>bigbit
<Content>Nadia is N-I-C-E I was there with my wife and a group of friends. We had 3 rooms total. two doubles and a single. I am from the USA and they were from UK. We stayed a total of 7 days and some had to leave in 4 days.I had a very nice room, although small as all Amsterdam Hotels are unless you are willing to pay 200 euro per night. I also must add the only time you will go to the room is to sleep and how much room is necessary for that. There is a safe in the room and a hairdryer. It was a bit dark and I asked for a lamp and it was delivered. They advertised wireless internet but at first it wasn't working. I must say that the owner/manager along with some outside help worked around the clock to make it work perfectly. So if wireless is what you need they have it and it was fast.The room was clean and we had a beautiful view of the canal with windows that opened, that made it even better as the church bells were very pleasant to listen to. The room was cleaned every day and the entire staff was very friendly. The beds were comfortable and the pillows just the way I like them. I felt very much at ease and comfortable here. The same 7 days at a few other places were 800+ euros and we went and looked at them. We found that we were winners at 650 euro. The only bad part of the whole experience is the steep steps, but if steps don't bother you as they didn't our 40-50 yr old group, then you won't have a problem. It was sort of an experience and a good laugh when you see the steps. Also if you like hot breakfast go across the street to Jennifers and tell the gentleman running the place you want Over easy Eggs like Angelo as he now knows what they are. Please Tell the Nadia owner Angelo, sends his regards. I will stay there again!!!

<Author>yannie
<Content>fresh fowers and friendly faces Having been warned about the steep staircase on the Nadia website it was still a surprise. However, we were met before we had ascended by a friendly young man who took our luggage. Tess on reception performed the official signing in routine with ease and directed us to the flower festooned breakfast room where we were given a welcome drink. Our room was tiny with 2ft 6inch twin beds and shower room. Functional and adequate except for insufficient lighting. Much appreciated were the small fridge, safe, telephone and tea/coffee facilities. Breakfasts were self service continental style with toast on request and drinks served with the familiar Nadia charm. On departure our luggage was stored until we were ready to be transported to the airport. Again we were directed to the breakfast room where we were plied with offers of refreshment. The staff carried our luggage down to the pavement and wished us a safe and pleasant journey.To sum up the Nadia in one sentence; a clean and friendly hotel suited to the more energetic slim visitor. Jean and Annie.

<Author>antp
<Content>Perfect location Just spent a prolonged week-end in Amsterdam. We are a family of 5 - 2 adults and 3 children aged 11, 15 and 17 - and Hotel Nadia was absolutely perfect for this purpose. With a very central location we had most of the sightseeing within walking distance, Anne Franks house across the street, shopping and strolling in the nine streets just around the corner and very good restaurants at reasonable prices on the other side of the canal in Jordaan. We booked our rooms on the website and a with a phonecall in advance we were sure of rooms on the same floor - with a special view for the two old ones. <Author>brushman333
<Content>Decent, but limited I recently stayed at the Nadia for several nights. First, I'll say that I'm a seasoned business traveler, and have been to Amsterdam 11 times, so this is not my first small hotel expereince in the city.I arrived around 10am. No one offered to help me up the very steep stairs to the lobby which is one floor above street level. The staff was always very nice and helpful. I was offered coffee or tea if I wanted, and they checked my bags, advising the room would not be available until 1pm. More very steep stairs up to my room. Facing the steepness of the stairs was a real drag after a long day of walking around the city. If you don't have alot of stamina, skip this place. Yes, these stairs are steeper than any I've encountered in Amsterdam.My room was cramped, even by Amsterdam standards. The bedspread was torn and had burn holes, the sheets were clean, but had a rip in it. I did not receive fresh towels for several days - the staff would simply fold up the used towels and place them back on the rack. This was annoying as I was only given one hand towel and one bath towel, as a single guest. I found myself hitting my head on shelves, and banging my shin on the bed platform more often than I care to admit, as the room was so tight. As mentioned in other reviews, the toilet is in the shower. My toilet seat cover could not be lowered, nor could the seat be lifted, due to it being wedged between the toilet tank (hard to describe). This led to constant risk of items falling into the open toilet from the miniscule glass shelf above, the only place in the bathroom for your personal toiletries. The room was on the back of the hotel facing a courtyard, and was mostly quiet, with the exception of hearing the church bells of the Westerkerk through the night (this was very pleaseant, actually). Some of the nights were warm, so I had the window open. Apparently the reception desk also faced the courtyard some floors below, as on a couple of nights I was kept awake by the constant piercing ring of the reception desk telephone, echoing up the courtyard at all hours. Why the management doesn't either lower the volume, change the type of ringer (a flashing light perhaps?), or simply keep the window shut so as to not disturb the guests, is beyond me.I'd say the Nadia is an okay place to stay if you're not bothered by what I've mentioned. The location is very good for getting around the city (close to 3 tram lines, Canal Bus and Dam Square), there's an ATM across the street, and an internet cafe a block away. I feel the price was high for the room. I won't be staying at the Nadia again.  
<Date>Sep 15, 2006

Stairs are very steep!Staff were all very friendly and the breakfast was basic but fine.The only negative aspect was an odd smell in our room that was noticeable when entering from outside. We had to ignore it with the help of air fresheners. Our friends were in the next room which was odour free.If you just want somewhere to sleep and shower, the Nadia is just about ideal.

<Author>hemikiwi
<Content>Mixed Feelings but have to remember it is a 2 star hotel Unfortunately, I arrived in Amsterdam at a time when all my favourite hotels were full due to a conference. I eventually had to go to the Tourist Information to book a room. Even here, rooms were full due to a conference in town. Whilst I was there, a phone call came in from Hotel Nadia due to a cancellation. I was offered a double room for 100euro. I agreed as I needed a bed for the night. The Hotel is situated quite centrally but in a rather grubby road. The staircase to reception needs to be seen to be believed....i have seen many steep staircases in Amsterdam but this was steeeeeeep!!!! However, an employee ( you are buzzed in from reception) came down and carried my bag upstairs. You are then greeted by reception and offered a free cold drink ! My double  room had a double bed , space for clothing, a tv, and tiny bathroom. I was grateful to find a room due to the conference so i was happy to be there. However, for 100euro plus booking fee it was definately overpriced. As a budget / 2 star hotel it was perfectly fine and as I normally stay in more upmarket hotels i know i need to be careful of my expectations. However, i still think 100 euro plus booking fee was overpriced for the quality of the room.My only complaint would be that there was a lot of noise coming from the restaurant / breakfast room late at night.Staff were very friendly , room overpriced for a 2 star budget hotel but if i had been lucky enough to get a good deal , i would not have any complaints apart from noise from through the wall.

<Author>AnneJones
<Content>Excellent service  Just stayed for 3 nights at the Hotel Nadia, which I'd booked after reading some of the reviews posted on this site. On first arrival the doorway is a bit uninviting with a buzzer, (oh yes the tram stop is Westerkirk, it's really easy to find from the station)but at least you feel a bit secure because they buzz you in each time so people aren't just wandering in. And yes the stairs are really scary looking but you do get used to them, although any one with mobility difficulties would not manage them. The room we first stayed in was a twin room at the back of the hotel, but I'm afraid I couldn't cope with the claustrophobic feeling it gave me and the manager was really understanding and we managed to move rooms. The rooms are small, but very clean and the sheets and beds are comfy, and the room service is excellent. Obviously if you are looking to spend a lot of time in your room you may find it negative re the size of the rooms, but if it is a city break or you are not bothered too much about the room size, then I would recommend it. The location is good and we walked most places and also took the trams. I cannot praise the staff enough and they were extremely friendly and helpful and I would definitely go back again! And one last thing the coffee is really good that they serve for breakfast!!

<Content>great 2 week stay My husband and I stayed there 2 weeks and it was great. You wont be staying alot of time in any hotel, but some days you want to rest. The people there are so helpfull and nice. There are the steps that yes are a killer, but they do help you with your luggage and you get used them fast for you have alot of walking do to. Staying there you are close to everything. We did have are clothes washed and they do charge a fee. If you need anything they do it or really try for you. We had a great time and plan to go back. It was great for the price and we didnt go for a big fansy place. We got what we wanted bed, private bathroom, t.v. phone, frig, and a bed for two. November was great weather and we could put the heat on and leave the window open. The bells are not a big bother, I liked them. You do have to leave you keys everytime you leave, and they buzz you when you come back. There is no vistors allowed, and I liked that, no one running around. Breakfast is nice, not American, but you get a nice breakfast and dont have to spend more money. All in all we plan to go back and stay there again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A great find! I really loved this hotel. It's pretty basic but this is more than made up for by the fantastic service and incredibley homely atmosphere the owners and staff provide. When we arrived, we had been up since 3am as we had caught the early morning flight from liverpool. It was freezing cold, sleety and windy when we arrived in amsterdam but the welcome we received at the Nadia really cheered us all up. Once we had navigated the notorious stairs (we left our bags in the ahll and the staff brought them up for us - thank God!)we were warmly welcomed at reception. We were there before our rooms were ready so the owner sat us in the breakfast room with a pile of brochures and booklets and kept our mugs of free coffee full until our rooms were ready. The rooms are tiny but so well laid out that they have everything you need and more. The rooms even have fridges which I know from staying in Amsterdam several times before is very rare, expecially for a 3*. The location is good, right by the Anne Frank museum on Prinsengracht and only a few minutes walk from Dam Square. Also, our favourite coffeeshop (La Tertulia) is just around the corner so this is another bonus! Breakfast is simple continental style - croissants, pastries, fruit, ham, cheese, toast, jam etc. with lots of fruit juice and cosntant refills of freshly made coffee from (I think) the owner's wife, who is really friendly and funny. I've read other reviews on here complaining about the room size and I imagine if you want to sit around all day in a big spacious 5* hotel for your visit, then you will be disappointed with the Nadia. If, like us, however you just want a base to sleep and eat breakfast with great, warm, friendly service, I highly recommend the Nadia. I'm already planning my next trip!  
<Date>Jan 3, 2006

<Author>croesio
<Content>Cheap, clean and friendly. Great situation, within easy walking distance of all the major sites.The entrance is just a single doorway and the stairs to the reception area are the steepest I've ever seen! However we did not have to carry our luggage up or down these stairs.We vacated out room on the morning of departure and the luggage was left in our room until it was put into our taxi when we left the hotel.We also got a free welcome drink when we reached reception on the first day!The staff are very friendly and helpful and all speak English.The rooms are very small and hot. We left our window open at all times and the traffic is very noisy throughout the night. The bathroom is also tiny but the shower was very good. As we only spent a short time in our rooms this did not matter too much.We did not bother to unpack our suitcases as the room was too small for a wardrobe. Breakfast was basic - croissants,toast,cheese, jams, coffee -but it was adequate.We found the restaurants in the immediate vicinity of the hotel tended to close about 10.30pm and the first night we did not realise that there were plenty of places off Dam Square that stayed open much later.A great little hotel but I would prefer a bigger room next time.

<Author>Richieh
<Content>Not a bad little place! Even after all the warnings on this site I wasn't prepared for the stair case leading to the first floor reception! It was negotiable but take care as even the treads on the steps are very narrow. I went with 4 friends and we booked into the Nadia 2 hours early due to the early flight arrival. Our luggage was placed into a 'baggage storage area' immediately after the simple booking in procedure. This baggage area was nothing more than a small alcove with a curtain so don't leave anything too valuable there. It's location in the city is ideal and close to some very good restaurants and bars. Get the train directly from the airport (Schipol) to centraal station. Come out of the main station entrance and head down 'Damrak', at the monument turn right and go over a couple of narrow canals. The hotel is on the corner of 'Raadhuistraat' but make sure you look for the hotel sign as the entrance is a single doorway. The staff are really polite and helpful. This was the case when I thought I'd lost my passport. They put me straight onto the British consulate. As with the other reviews the rooms we had were tiny. Ours was supposed to be a triple but would have been better described as a small twin. If you're chlaustraphobic you wont be impressed so if this bothers you, pay a little more for a hotel with larger rooms. All in all a reasonable hotel for the price in a good location. I wouldn't personally use it again but only because the rooms are so small. The staff and location are great. Fantastic city, wonderful accommodating Dutch people who made a great effort to make 5 'Brit tourists very happy. Hoping to make our booking to Amsterdam for early next year very soon.

<Author>Canadian2007
<Content>Good hotel for the money I stayed at the Nadia for 3 nights in September, 2005. Yes - the staircase is very steep, and the rooms are tiny. But its centrally located, the rooms are clean and the staff are extremely friendly and helpful (they even have unbrellas you can borrow should it rain during your stay). I had a room on the front so the traffic noice could have been a problem, but a pair of earplugs solved that, and the little balcony with a view of the Westerkirk more than made up for the noise. Anne Frank House is just around the corner, the Dam is a 3 minute walk, and the tram stop is just up the street. I had a single room on the same floor as reception and the breakfast room - room came complete with cable TV, a safe, coffee and tea makings, and a very tiny, spotlessly clean private bathroom - all for only 55 Euros a night. Breakfast is served from 7:30 to 10:00 - simple continental breakfast of croissants, bread, marble cake, juice and really good coffee, in a comfortable although very small, breakfast room.And regarding those stairs - I asked and was told that no guest has ever fallen down them yet! All in all, its a good hotel for the money.

<Content>Disappointing We booked this hotel based upon some reasonable reviews. Sadly, it turned out to be a big disppointment. It appears that some of the more recent (poor) reviews are more reflective of the true standard of this hotel. Our room was small but since we spent most of the day sightseeing, this was no real problem. More importantly, the room was incredibly worn and dingy. Also, the shower did not work properly. Overall, the hotel is badly in need of some refurbishment and is very over rated on this site. I've given it a two star rating because it is relatively cheap, the location is not bad and the staff were reasonably friendly. However, I would certainly try somewhere else next time.

<Author>Belfasttravellers
<Content>Overall a good hotel. Our party of three stayed in the Hotel Nadia in June 2005. We booked a double room and a single for four nights. This hotel is in a central location, easy to locate (just around the corner from Dam Square) and is about a 15 minute walk from the Central Railway Station.This hotel has some good points and some bad points. As with most hotels in Amsterdam, the staircase is quite steep. When you enter the hotel, there are 35 stairs to climb to the reception area. We were given a complimentary drink when we arrived. We warmly welcomed and checked in.The double room (which was actually two single beds pushed together) appeared to be clean and tidy. There was a fridge, tea and coffee facilities (which were not replenished as they were used), a desk with 2 chairs, a TV with 4 channels (not cable as advertised) and a VERY compact bathroom. The bathroom in our double room was actually a shower room with a toilet and a basin in it. The bathroom did omit an odour (an unpleasant sewer smell which could sometimes be smelt in the room). The single room had a queen size double bed (small double) which sppeared to be clean and tidy. There was a fridge, a desk with 1 chair, a TV with satelite/cable channels. There was no tea/coffee making facilities. There was an ample sized bathroom with a separate shower. Both of these rooms faced the front of the hotel, and therefore noise from trams and buses from the street could be heard at night which sometimes made it difficult to sleep. A breakfast consisting of croissants bread, cheese, marble cake, selection of jams and honey, tea and coffee and fresh orange juice which is served between 8am - 11am in the cosy breakfast room.We very much enjoyed our stay at Hotel Nadia. My only complaint was the alkward bathroom (which sometimes smelt). The absence of cable TV in our room didn't bother us because we came to enjoy the city, not watch TV. As many other people on Tripadvisor have said, the hotel is small as most Amsterdam hotels tend to be, but lets face it, if you see your hotel room as someplace clean to sleep and wash, it isnt a problem. If you want a larger room, then look for a 3/4 star hotel. If you are considering staying at this hotel, also check out Hotel Boheme.  
<Date>Jul 3, 2005

<Author>neitzjl
<Content>Good Hotel for the Price We stayed at the Hotel Nadia one night while we were in Amsterdam. The location was central in the city and about a 15 minute walk from the train station. The staff was very friendly and helpful. Everyone spoke good English. They gave us complimentary water at check-in and then again when we got back later that night after checking out the Red Light District. The room was comically small but clean and quiet. The breakfast was average ( a typical European breakfast with croissants, bread, cheese, juice, and coffee). However the stairs in the hotel are quite step and there are plenty of them. This was not a problem for us but I would not recommend this hotel for anybody who is elderly or at all physically disabled. We would defintely stay here again as it was nearly half the price as other hotels in Amsterdam and very acceptable.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A nice hotel. My fianc茅 and I stayed at Hotel Nadia this past weekend while in Amsterdam celebrating my 30th birthday.The hotel is located just a few minutes walk from Dam Square, which makes getting around easy. There are several tram stops near the hotel as well.When you open the front door to the hotel you will be astounded by the stairs that lead up to the reception, the 2 flights of stairs that go straight up! So this is defiantly not a hotel for anyone who has trouble climbing stairs, as they are a bit steep.Once we made it up the stair, we were given a warm welcome and a nice cold welcome drink and assigned our room. Which was on the 4th floor, so up we went 2 more flights of steep stairs.The room we had was the standard room which over looked nothing in particular as it was at the back of the building. At first I thought I wanted to try to get a canal room, but realized that the traffic noise probably would have bothered me.Now the room is very small and basic but it is clean and comfortable. Our bathroom was the same. It is basically a large shower room, so no romantic baths. My only complaint was that the hotel lacks air conditioning, which would have been nice one the really warm nights. My second complaint, which has nothing to do with the hotel, was about the church nearby that rang it's bells all through the night, so it made sleeping with the window open a bit of a pain.Over all we had a great stay. The staff was lovely, recommending a fantastic seafood restaurant to eat at, and always making sure we knew where we were going when heading out. The hotel may be small but it is clean. So if you don't care much for the trappings of a posh hotel, then stay here.

<Author>Jen1978
<Content>Besy hotel in Amsterdam! I've been to Amsterdam several times and have had different degrees of luck with the various hotels I've sampled there. The Nadia is by far and away the nicest hotel I've stayed in in the city. I booked it after reading the reviews on here. It is fantastic value for money, cosy, friendly and centrally located. The rooms are tiny (like cabins) but have everything you need. The staff are the nicest people you could hope to meet and nothing was to much trouble for them. As for the stairs.....they are overwhelming when you first open the front door and see the receptionist peering down from miles away up on the first floor but we were instructed to leave our bags in the hall and staff quickly brougt them up to our rooms. I notice someone on here was complaining about having to wait for their room to be ready - we had a wait too but the staff escort you to the dining room and offer you free hot or cold drinks so it's hardly a hardship! Breakfast is a simple continental spread - lovely raisin toast, croissants, cheese and great coffee! - and the dining rom is really cosy like the rest of the hotel.Will definitely be staying here again.

<Author>downinit
<Content>Great location, great value I booked this hotel after reading all the positive reviews, and I was not disappointed. The price and location are very hard to beat(~70 Euro and right by Dam/Anne Frank/tram stop). The rooms were very small, as to be expected in the Amsterdam city center area, but there was sufficient room for more luggage than 2 people should ever need, which is what we had. The bed was nice and soft, and the room/bathroom was clean and well-kept. The reception was also very friendly. The only problems I had, which would not keep me from staying here again, were the stairwell was narrow and very steep, not to mention long, but what else would u expect in the land of narrow canal houses. Its not too bad as long as u are healthy, but the elderly and disabled would find it very difficult, especially loaded with luggage. Also the closest tram stop goes right in front of the hotel and stops a block over, in front of a church, but if you are not paying attention to the area, and dont have a very detailed map, you may not notice that the street changes names between the hotel and the tram stop. This, combined with a hotel map printed online, led us to walk in a big circle around a large block, when all we had to do was walk the other way 100 feet from the tram to the hotel. But this is more of a warning to those who choose to stay here, and by no means a complaint against the hotel, which I highly recommend as a tourist class hotel. Its not the Ritz, but its much cheaper, and nicer than many 3 star hotels I've been to.

<Author>nathsal
<Content>Super little hotel in a great location! This is a super little budget hotel in a great location for Amsterdam. First impressions is just a doorway between shops, behind which are the steepest stairs i've ever seen! However, the very friendly staff will help you with any luggage and give you a complimentary drink to recover!I have to say that it was also the smallest room i have ever stayed in with approx one foot of space around the double bed which was pushed up against the window! However, it had absolutely everything we could have wished for... tv, fridge, safe, shelves and radiator all clinging precariously to the walls! It had a small but adequate wardrobe and a minute but clean shower/wc. We also requested a canal view room with a balcony and were lucky enough to be given one by the lovely hotel owner. The balcony offered lovely views of the Westerkerk church and canal one way and the rear of the Grand Palace at Dam Square the other. The rooms viewing the road could be a bit noisy with the chimes of the church and a tram stop outside but it never bothered us.As mentioned the nadia hotel is in a great location, minutes from Ann Frank's house, the red light district and Dam Square and is easily walkable from the Centraal train Station.If you want a budget, central hotel then we would highly recommend hotel Nadia and we would definitely stay here again.  
<Date>Feb 25, 2005

<Author>Chris_Halford
<Content>Great Little Hotel I stopped at the Nadia Hotel after reading good reviews on the internet. I was not disappointed, the Hotel is as many others say very friendly and extremely clean. The staff cannot do too much for even down to a welcome drink.It's in a good location about 5 minutes from Dam Square and located on the corner of the canal looking over the Westerkerk Church.The rooms are on the small side but all have an individual feel about them, not like the normal standardised layout you normally get in Hotels. Ours had both a balcony and a view looking over the church.The only downside is the steep stairs and this would be difficult if you have problems with them. The staff however are very quick to help carry luggage around.Would I stay there again - definately. Can I recommend it - Yes (I've stopped at the prestigous Die Port Van Cleve Hotel and its rooms were worst). Is it value for money - Yes.Have at look at their web site for a better feel. It accurately reflects what you will get. ------------

<Author>hazel
<Content>great service! The thing that makes the place special has to be the staff. We were offered arrival drinks and luckily our luggage was taken to our room so we didn't have to struggle up the stairs. We had a double room with a balcony - large it wasn't but the balcony helped. Bit noisy being on a main tramway, but these stop running at 1am. Breakfast was a simple affair - cheese slices, sliced bread and cakes, croissants (if you're quick), jams etc. Would recommend Nadia for the location too - Amsterdam is easy to get round on foot and the hotel was very close to Dam Square, Anne Frank House etc. We had a lovely time at Nadia - it's not five star but perfectly adequate for a long weekend break.

<Author>lareu
<Content>Small and Friendly Stayed here four nights, Sept. 3-6, 2004. Good location next to the Westerkerk. First thing you will notice is the stairs, very steep, quite a climb. Second thing you will likely notice is how friendly the staff is (all of those that I encountered) and I was greeted with a welcome drink. Postage stamp size single room, very clean. Shower was really just a corner of the bathroom with a curtain but adequately functional. Apparatus to make coffee or tea in the room as well as a safe. Breakfast included in price of the room, various breads, cheese, coffee and juices. Booked a single room for 50 euros for my sister who was to arrive from Florida, but a hurricane prevented her departure from Miami. I didn鈥檛 know until way past the cancellation deadline, but the hotel staff felt bad and didn鈥檛 charge me for her room. That was nice of them. If you don鈥檛 mind a small room it is a good choice for the budget traveler and the staff will make you feel welcome.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>'Excellent hotel on a budget' Stayed two nights with husband and daughter, location was fantastic - you are in the centre of it all. We were aware of the steps as it was highlited before booking but it made the hotel even more like a typical 'Amsterdam' house. For what you pay, the rooms were as expected. As for the staff, well they were EXCEPTIONAL!!! We even got invited to a small family gathering as it was the owners birthday party which included a cake to be shared out. Our daughter thought it was the best thing ever!! If you want genuine hospitality then definitely stay here. Without a doubt we shall return on our next trip. The only downside for us was the noisy traffic throughout the night, but then we did book a budget room and our room was overlooking the main street.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Warm  I've just got back from a lovely weekend in Amsterdam. We stayed at the Nadia Hotel and were very pleasantly suprised. The first thing you see when you open the door is a massive steep staircase. Immediately, the receptionist shouted down for us to leave our luggage at the bottom and someone would bring it up for us. We weren't due to check in until 1pm (we arrived about 9.30am), but they were so welcoming and invited us to help ourselves to breakfast in the dining area. The staff were lovely and friendly and I found the whole experience enjoyable.The hotel is perfectly located next to the westerkerk (you can hear the bells chime) just round the corner fromt he Anne Frank House (well worth a visit). We found the location to be fairly central to all parts of the city.Although the room was small, it was clean and comfortable.All in all, I would highly recommend this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Really friendly and helpful staff I went with 3 of my friends, we found that the staff were really helpful and friendly. The stairs up to reception were a little steap but not really a problem and the toilet/shower was a little cramped but everything else was really good. Breakfast from about 7.30am to 10.30am allows you plenty of time to get something to eat. The location of the hotel is excellent, right by the center of amsterdam and just 10 minutes walk to most places!! For what you pay, it really was good. The rooms are nice, they have a fridge, t.v with cable and a safe. I will definetly go back to the hotel when i go back to amsterdam.
